US Prepares to Increase Defenses in the Pacific After Naval Negotiations Fail

Congressional Members Plan to Introduce Bill

Establish Invincible Naval Port in Alaska

Government Still Hopes for Compromise with Japan Despite Restraint

(Washington) The Associated Press learned today from reliable sources that the United States still hopes to conclude a new naval treaty within 1936. Senior government officials solemnly stated that although the United States is disappointed with the results of the initial talks in London, it still believes that future circumstances may be conducive to extending the naval treaty. The government does not intend to say much or take any action to provoke other countries' animosity towards the naval issue. Those close to the government indicate that now is not the appropriate time for Americans to harshly criticize the actions of other countries involved in the naval dispute, fearing that this would provoke retaliatory criticism from other countries. The repeated solemn expression of this compromising attitude is intended to offset the blunt expressions of congressional members and the discussion of establishing naval bases after Japan announced its abrogation of the naval treaty. (National Telegram on the 21st)

(Washington) It was learned today that the next session of Congress will recommend the construction of an invincible port and powerful military and air stations in Alaska. This proposal was put forward by Representative Dimond of Alaska in the House of Representatives. Dimond announced today that when the next session of Congress convenes, he will introduce two bills requesting congressional approval of appropriations for the construction of land and naval military defenses in the near future. Dimond advocates establishing military and air stations on the Alaskan mainland, far from the sea, so they are beyond the reach of naval artillery. This air base will house at least one hundred aircraft of various types. Dimond also stated that he will request the opening of a powerful naval base in Alaska or the Aleutian Islands. This matter can proceed after Japan abrogates the naval treaty. Dimond further stated that the naval base he proposes will be at least as solid as Pearl Harbor, the American naval fortress in Hawaii. Dimond predicts that his plan will definitely receive the support of a majority of members of Congress. Dimond also advocates digging the Nicaraguan Canal, because the defenses of the Panama Canal are insufficient. (National Telegram on the 21st)

(Washington) American public opinion generally believes that after Japan's abrogation of the Washington Treaty, the United States will no longer be bound by Article 19 of the treaty, which prohibits increasing defenses in the Pacific. The question of whether the Philippines should be independent will also be raised in conjunction. Although the government has remained silent on this issue, it is generally known that the government has always recognized that political and military issues in the Pacific are closely related. In addition, some liberals in the United States have another argument that while increasing American national defense is necessary, if it is only used as a means to implement the Open Door Policy in China by developing the American navy, it is feared that the United States will be constrained and fall into a dangerous path. Conversely, it would be a big mistake for people to think that the Chinese market is insignificant to American interests. It is now believed that Yamamoto, the chief Japanese expert, will not stay in London for long. He may not be able to make Britain succumb to Japan's views. On the contrary, a compromise between Britain and the United States is currently even closer. It is also generally believed that Germany and the Soviet Union will be invited to attend the next formal naval conference to jointly participate in talks on Pacific issues. (Havas Telegram on the 21st)

Two Telegrams Issued from Tokyo

Unanimity of Matsudaira and Saito

Navy Declares the Main Purpose of Abrogating the Treaty

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota met with the Emperor at 10:35 this morning and submitted a memorial to approve the notification of the abrogation of the Washington Treaty decided by yesterday's cabinet meeting. After obtaining the Emperor's approval, Foreign Minister Hirota immediately sent a telegram to Saito, the Japanese ambassador to the United States, this afternoon, ordering him to hand over the notification to US Secretary of State Hull on the 27th. (United Press of China Telegram on the 22nd)

(Tokyo) Japan's response to the British proposal was telegraphed by Foreign Minister Hirota to Ambassador Matsudaira at 2:00 pm on the 23rd, instructing him to continue talks with Britain after Christmas. The content directly requests the realization of Japan's disarmament policy and principles. If the British government agrees, then after the resumption of informal meetings or preparatory talks, the British proposal on achieving equality can be considered. The first Anglo-Japanese negotiations after the recess seem to begin on the 27th or 28th of this month. (United Press of Japan Telegram on the 22nd)

(Tokyo) Domestic procedures for the notification of the abrogation of the Washington Treaty were completed today. Ambassador Saito to the United States was instructed by Foreign Minister Hirota. The Navy, considering today's great significance, issued the following statement in the form of an official statement to domestic and foreign audiences regarding the main purpose of the abrogation:

(1) Thirteen years have passed since the conclusion of the Washington Treaty. During this period, due to scientific progress, warships, weapons, and aircraft have developed extraordinarily, and the international situation has also changed extraordinarily, making it unsuitable for today's situation, and it will cause defects in Japan's future national defense. Therefore, taking the opportunity of the expiration date of Showa 11 (1936), we have decided to terminate the notification of abrogation. Domestic procedures have been completed today. (2) Japan does not expect a treaty-less state from this, but intends to conclude a fair and appropriate new treaty. The national effort to make this known is a well-known fact. At the disarmament conference, Japan earnestly hopes to abolish the ratio between the United States, Britain, and Japan, and set the maximum common amount of possession for each country, attempting to completely abolish or greatly reduce offensive military power, and implement the consolidation of defensive military power, so as to realize the principle of not threatening or invading, and to ensure the security of each country's national defense, so as to contribute to the establishment of world peace, which is sincerely hoped for. (3) In short, the abrogation of the Washington Treaty is for the further advancement of this purpose, and is merely the exercise of the rights under the treaty. (Dentsu Telegram on the 22nd)

Japan Establishes National Policy Deliberation Council to Deal with Emergencies

Begins Drafting Concrete Plan

Political Support and Opposition Attitudes

(Tokyo) As a result of the meeting of Finance Minister Takahashi, Commerce Minister Machida, and Communications Minister Tokonami, the problem of establishing the National Policy Deliberation Council was decided as follows:

(1) The National Policy Deliberation Council is an organization for establishing national policy with the consensus of the whole country. (2) The National Policy Deliberation Council is a permanent organization. (3) If a person with authority is appointed as a long-term member, a powerful national policy will be established. (4) The National Policy Deliberation Council will establish important national policies in various fields such as national defense, diplomacy, finance, economy, and industry. (5) A specialized committee will be established, attached to the National Policy Deliberation Council, and will gather authorities from various ministries as its members. (United Press of Japan Telegram on the 22nd)

(Tokyo) The outline of the concrete plan for the National Policy Deliberation Council is as follows: (1) The Prime Minister will serve as the chairman of the council, and the members will be senior statesmen, representatives of both houses of parliament, and 12 or 13 major figures from the financial and academic communities. It will serve as a consultation organization for finance, administration, and economy. (2) A large-scale investigation organization will be established within the deliberation council, with 40 or 50 authoritative figures as members, to be responsible for investigation and research. Yoshida, Chief Secretary, and Kanamori, Director-General of the Legislation Bureau, have begun drafting a concrete plan. (Reuters Telegram on the 22nd)

(Tokyo) The Seiyukai is paying close attention to the government's establishment of the National Policy Deliberation Council. The attitude of the executives is generally as follows: Diplomacy and national defense should be operated according to the policies of Foreign Minister Hirota and Army Minister Hayashi. At a time when external criticism cannot be tolerated, setting up a deliberation council is only a mechanism for the government to evade responsibility, and on the contrary, there is a risk of causing political operations to fall into error. The purpose of the government's eagerness to set up this organization is to disrupt the Seiyukai, so the Seiyukai will continue its policy of not sending cabinet members to the current cabinet. Those who participate in the deliberation council through individual negotiations will be expelled. (Dentsu Telegram on the 22nd)

Founding Company Jointly Operated by Japan and Puppets

(3) The immigration areas are first set as Hulin, Mishan, Huachuan, Baoqing, Boli and other counties. Truth of the Kirov Case Comes to Light

The Murderer is a Member of a Terrorist Group

Purpose is to Overthrow the Current Government

Trotskyists are the Initiators

(Moscow) Officials here announced today that Nikolaiyev, the murderer of Kirov, and thirteen people related to the Zinoviev opposition party have been sent to military institutions and the Supreme Court for disposition, charged with conspiring to assassinate Central Executive Committee member Kirov. Kirov was regarded by many as Stalin's right-hand man. The fourteen were also accused of taking terrorist actions against senior Soviet Russian officials in order to overthrow the Soviet Russian government, that is, hoping to replace Stalin with Trotsky and Zinoviev to control the Soviet Russian government. Zinoviev was arrested on Thursday at the same time as Kamenev, and is now in custody. Kamenev was also a former leader of the Communist Party. The government stated today that the fourteen people who were arrested had all been expelled from the Communist Party, but several of them, such as Zinoviev and Miganiev, were allowed to participate in party affairs again after renouncing their opposition. Among them, Zinoviev was the most prominent. Zinoviev was newly appointed as Deputy Minister of Education a few days before his arrest. Zinoviev had been expelled twice before for supporting Trotsky. (National Telegram on the 22nd)

(London) Soviet Russian Dictator Stalin has suggested to France that Trotsky be expelled, because Trotsky initiated various rebellions, and the assassination of Kirov was only the beginning of his conspiracy. This news was telegraphed to London by the Daily Express correspondent in Warsaw. The telegram also stated that Stalin will personally interrogate Zinoviev, the former Secretary-General of the Third International, Kamenev, the former Soviet Russian Ambassador to Turkey, and the other twelve people who were arrested in connection with the assassination of Kirov. The telegram went on to say that the trial is about to be held, and if the arrested people are proven guilty, they will all be executed by firing squad. (National Telegram on the 22nd)

(Moscow) The preliminary hearing of the Kirov assassination case ended yesterday. The various materials have been handed over to the Military Collegium of the Supreme Court of the Soviet Union. The preliminary hearing proved that Nikolaiyev, the murderer of Kirov on December 1, was a member of a secret terrorist group. The group was established in Leningrad, and its members were all former Zinoviev oppositionists. Nikolaiyev committed the murder in order to execute the instructions issued by the "Leningrad Center" of the secret terrorist group. The instructions were issued by the leader of the center, Kotolinov. The preliminary hearing proved that the motive for Kirov's murder was that the secret anti-Soviet group wanted to disintegrate the leadership of the Soviet government through the assassination of Soviet government leaders, thereby changing the current policy according to the so-called "Zinoviev-Lenin-Trotskyism". According to the murderer's confession, Kirov's assassination also had a retaliatory intent, because Kirov was the one who theoretically and politically destroyed the Leningrad Zinoviev faction. Nikolaiyev confessed, "In the past, the opposition always wanted to take his life because Kirov presided over the struggle against the anti-Leningrad opposition." The preliminary hearing also proved that this anti-Soviet group was extremely weak, and had despaired of gaining popular support, and had no political outlet. They were adopting terrorist means because they could not achieve their goals. The "Leningrad Center" of the secret terrorist group included members Kotolinov, Shatsky, Lunyantuv, Mandelshtamm, Misnikov, Levin, Susitsky, and Nikolaiyev. They were all former Zinoviev oppositionists. In addition, Sokolov, Svetlov, Yustkin, Antonov, Hannik, and Tolmachev were also arrested, and have been sent to the Military Collegium of the Supreme Court of the Soviet Union for investigation in accordance with the orders of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union. The above-mentioned figures had all been expelled from the party for participating in the activities of the Zinoviev opposition in the past, but most of them regained their party membership after formally declaring their willingness to obey the party and the policies of the Soviet government. The murderer Nikolaiyev was expelled from the party in early 1934 for violating party rules. Two months later, Nikolaiyev rejoined the party after repenting. (TASS Telegram on the 21st)

Order Issued by the Saar Governing Commission to Prohibit Flag Displays

German Front Expresses Resistance

British Troops Welcomed During Transit Through France

Saar Residents Display Coldness Towards Italian Troops

Saarbrücken, Saar – The Saar Governing Commission today issued an order prohibiting the display of any kind of flag. However, this order has been resisted by the "German Front," which has urged residents to display German flags as a sign of protest. As a result, thousands of Nazi flags are currently flying from doors and windows in Saarbrücken. (Reuters, 22nd)

Calais – A contingent of British troops, including officers and soldiers numbering approximately one hundred, en route to the Saar via France, arrived here from Gatwick today. They were warmly welcomed by local authorities and the French population. As the British troops boarded the train to proceed to the Saar, onlookers shouted, "Long live England! Long live the British troops!" Three hundred and fifty Italian soldiers entered Saarbrücken today, but the spectators outside the station remained silent. One Saar resident made a cold remark, saying, "We didn't invite them here." This statement reflects the general attitude. The main body of British troops is expected to arrive in Saarbrücken from Calais tomorrow. Walwal Belongs to Abyssinian Territory

Explicit Stipulation in the Italo-Abyssinian Treaty

Abyssinian Minister to France Issues Statement

(Paris) – The Abyssinian Legation in France recently issued a statement asserting that the Walwal region, where the Italo-Abyssinian military conflict occurred, is not part of Italian Somaliland as claimed by the Italian side. According to the Italo-Abyssinian Treaty of 1908, Walwal is designated as part of the Abyssinian territory of the Ogaden province. Walwal is located in the center of Ogaden province, 400 kilometers from the coast, while the border of Italian Somaliland extends only to 300 kilometers from the coast. Therefore, it is clear that the area falls within Abyssinian territory. (Havas, 21st)

Chinese Silver Exports to the US

No Reduction Seen in the First Half of This Month

(Washington) – The Associated Press learned today that silver-supporting legislators from Western states are currently considering the possibility of a Congressional investigation into the Treasury Department's implementation of the Silver Purchase Act of 1934. Treasury Secretary Henry Morgenthau Jr.'s failure to disclose the extent of the Treasury Department's silver purchases in the international silver market has aroused suspicion among silver-supporting legislators, who believe that the Treasury Department has not been diligent in purchasing silver. However, the Congressional consensus on the silver issue will not take concrete form until other leaders arrive. Several senators who have arrived in Washington today stated that the demand for this investigation is unlikely to materialize, because there is internal disagreement among silver supporters. However, three prominent silver-supporting legislators are determined to challenge the Treasury Department and advocate that the Treasury Department should report to Congress on matters related to the following points: (1) the extent of silver purchases to date; (2) the impact of silver purchases on the economy; (3) the cost of silver purchases to date; (4) whether silver has been sold to curb rising silver prices. The Department of Commerce announced today that silver imports for the week ending December 14 showed a sharp decline compared to the previous week. Silver imports for this period amounted to only $1,244,949, compared to $2,053,501 for the week ending December 7. China remains the largest supplier of silver, providing $342,130 for this period, compared to $9,334 for the previous week. Chile is the second-largest supplier of silver, providing $328,858 for this period, compared to $86,463 for the previous week. Imports from Mexico amounted to $206,725, imports from Canada amounted to $161,217, and silver imports from the United Kingdom were minimal, whereas they were substantial in the previous week. (National Telegram, 21st)

Cause of Dutch Plane Crash

Mistaken Landing in a Swamp During a Thunderstorm

Aircraft Completely Destroyed, Seven Killed

Basra – Although the remains of passengers and crew of the Dutch aircraft are fragmented, they are still identifiable. The fuselage overturned and crashed to the ground, irreparably damaged. Letters are scattered around the plane, as the aircraft was carrying Christmas mail from Amsterdam to the Dutch East Indies, with a scheduled round trip of five days. The crash site is in a narrow valley with treacherous rocky mountains, so other aircraft cannot land. Only police vehicles can retrieve the remains. It is now speculated that the Dutch aircraft crashed because it encountered a thunderstorm at high altitude and was forced to land. Initially, it seemed to be landing on solid ground, but after heavy rain, it had become a swamp, and the plane suddenly overturned, broke apart, and caught fire. The mail has now been collected and sent to Rutbah, and the seven bodies on board have been sent to a desert station. (Reuters, 22nd)

Page 9

A Jurist Discusses the Amount of Appellate Interest in Civil Procedure Law

(Nanjing) – The recently passed Article 463 of the Civil Procedure Law by the Legislative Yuan stipulates that the amount of appellate interest shall not exceed 500 yuan and may be increased to 1,000 yuan. According to a jurist, given the general social and economic conditions in China, it would be more appropriate for the amount not to exceed 200 yuan. Taking the amount of property as the standard for enjoying the right of third instance is theoretically untenable. In order to understand the livelihood of the poor in our country, it is not appropriate to further increase the amount of interest. Although this case has been passed in the third reading, it is hoped that the central government will find ways to remedy it in order to protect the right of third instance for the poor. (Central News Agency, 22nd)

Important Cases Resolved by the Jiangsu Anti-Opium Association

(Zhenjiang) – The Jiangsu Provincial Anti-Opium Committee resolved on the 22nd: (1) If licensed smokers purchase and smoke private soil or supply opium to others, it will be regarded as private sales; (2) Each county's drug rehabilitation center will be issued 20 sets of cotton clothing; (3) Pass the regulations on rewards and punishments for anti-opium civil servants in the province, as well as the methods for drug rehabilitation centers in various counties to apply for soil acquisition for manufacturing medicinal liquor, and the training of large-scale investigation and suppression plans. Zeng Wanzhong represented the chairman and resolved the following major issues: (1) Establishing a winter defense committee; (2) Thoroughly investigating the household registration of the entire port; (3) Conducting regular major inspections; (4) Jointly defending the entire port with military and police forces divided into patrolling groups; (5) Setting the period from the end of this month to the end of next February as the winter defense period; (6) Emphasizing the inspection of stations and hotels; (7) Banning idle soldiers. A total of sixteen major issues, including the winter defense expenses borne by various agencies, were resolved. (22nd Central News Agency Telegram)

Korean People in Peiping Again Injure Police Officers

Strict Drug Prohibition Causes Hatred Among Koreans

Gathering to Assault Our Police Chief and Officers, etc.

Beijing Correspondence: Since the authorities in this city have strictly prohibited drugs, the Japanese-Korean people who are generally engaged in the business of selling white powder feel that their livelihoods are cut off and are greatly panicked. At first, they still hoped that our Party authorities would implement the ban on opium in the same way as in previous years, with lax enforcement, and that it would become a dead letter after the storm passed. Later, they saw that Chinese people who smoked and sold drugs were arrested and executed without any leniency, and even Korean houses could be inspected together with the Japanese police and arrested separately. Therefore, the drug-trafficking Koreans scattered in the nine cities felt disappointed and harbored hatred. Relying on the protection of the Japanese, they formed a united front, seeking ways to specifically antagonize our national police officers. In recent days, cases of Korean people assaulting police officers have occurred frequently, such as in the inner first district, inner second district, inner third district, and other areas. It is almost heard every day. Unexpectedly, one wave has not subsided, and another has risen. Yesterday (the 18th) late at night, on the border of the inner fourth district, another bizarre similar case occurred, and Patrol Officer Bai Changhui was severely injured. The details are recorded as follows:

Zhang Shizhe, a Korean resident at No. 10 Daxi Hutong, Nanshucheng Street, inside Fuchengmen, Peiping, is forty years old. He has been distributing white powder in the western city area for a long time and is considered quite wealthy. He employs many servants in his home, who are responsible for secretly transporting white powder. Since the city authorities

Page 10

implemented drug prohibition, the inner fourth district office immediately dispatched plainclothes detectives to patrol near the residence. If any Chinese people went to buy drugs, they would be arrested and sent to the bureau for legal action. Therefore, addicts generally regarded the residence as a dangerous place. Zhang Shizhe also felt that the authorities were so strict that it was tantamount to cutting off his life. Yesterday (the 18th) at 9 PM, he gathered more than 20 Korean people engaged in the drug trade in his home to discuss how to retaliate. At around 10 PM, two Chinese people happened to go to buy drugs. At this time, Zhang and the other Koreans had already conspired and planned properly. When the two Chinese people entered the house, Zhang immediately ordered all the Koreans and servants in the courtyard to step forward and tie them up. The two Chinese people, still considering themselves as old customers, were suddenly tied up and did not know what to do. Zhang then sent another Korean person to rush to the fourth section police station of the inner fourth district to report that bandits were openly robbing and asked them to come and arrest them. Police Chief Bai Changhui of the section immediately led more than ten police officers, including Cheng Yongli, to the residence to prepare to attack the bandits. Unexpectedly, after arriving at the residence, they saw two Chinese people lying on the ground, bound with ropes, and did not know what was going on. Many Koreans were standing beside them, holding wooden sticks, their expressions fierce. Police Chief Bai then asked Zhang where the bandits were and whether there had been any losses. Zhang not only did not answer but also questioned why the police district had abandoned its duties and did not provide prior protection. When Police Chief Bai was about to reply, Zhang shouted and ordered the Koreans holding wooden sticks to attack Police Chief Bai and all the police officers violently. Fortunately, Police Chief Bai and others understood the law deeply. Considering that the Koreans were foreigners and fearing that they contained a conspiracy to provoke on behalf of a certain party, they agreed to endure and not resist. At the same time, they immediately telegraphed the Public Security Bureau for assistance. At this time, police whistles were ringing loudly, and the police guarding Fuchengmen heard the news and rushed to the scene. Director Liu Zhenzhong also received a report and set off with officers Shi Binglin, clerk Che Junsheng, and many police officers at the same time. However, Police Chief Bai and police officer Cheng Yongli had already fallen to the ground due to injuries and were unconscious. Director Liu immediately questioned the people tied up on the ground. One person, Zhao Changyong, and another person, Xiao Wenying, both claimed to have come to buy white powder on behalf of a friend. Unexpectedly, they were tied up as soon as they entered the door and falsely accused of being robbers, etc. The injured police chief and two police officers had almost no intact skin on their heads, backs, and ribs. Their clothing was also torn. They were immediately carried back to the station for treatment. Zhao and Xiao were also taken to the station for interrogation, suspected of collusion. They were immediately transferred to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. It is reported that Yu Jinhe, Director of the Public Security Bureau, considered that the inside story of this case was complex and of great importance. He has submitted the entire case to the Municipal Government in detail and asked for instructions on future drug prohibition and how to deal with the Koreans. (20th)

Uses of Hubei Provincial Construction Bonds

To Build Southern and Western Hubei Highways

Hankou Correspondence: Governor Zhang Qun of Hubei Province plans to issue Hubei Provincial Construction Bonds to handle local construction and disaster relief. He sent Finance Director Jia Shiyi to Beijing to contact Minister Kong to discuss the bond amount of 6 million yuan, secured by the entire income from business tax and central government allocations. He also instructed the Finance Department to draft bond regulations and a principal and interest repayment schedule, which were submitted to the Provincial Government meeting for approval and scheduled to be issued on New Year's Day next year. After this plan was submitted to the Executive Yuan, it was sent to the Ministry of Finance for review, clearly stipulating that it would be used to build the Yunzhu, Shiba, and Shiyi highways in western Hubei Province, and the highways connecting Hunan and Jiangxi in southern Hubei Province. It was also scheduled to be issued on New Year's Day next year. According to responsible officials in the Finance Department, these bond regulations still need to be approved by the Central Political Conference and then passed by the Legislative Yuan before they can be promulgated and take effect. There are not many days left before New Year's Day next year. The bond certificates have not yet been printed, so it will be difficult to issue them as scheduled, but the delay will not be too long. The designated highway lines are all related to bandit suppression military affairs. If the construction is completed, the mountainous areas of western Hubei Province can become a thoroughfare, and the border areas of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces can be connected. At the same time, disaster victims can be employed for work relief, which is of great benefit. (21st)

City Autonomy Law and Implementation Law Passed by the Legislative Yuan

The City Autonomy Law and the City Autonomy Implementation Law were discussed and approved by the Legislative Yuan at its 85th meeting on the 18th of this month, according to the original draft in the second reading and amended. The chairman designated five members, including Huang Youchang, to reorganize the text and submit it to the meeting for discussion. Yesterday (the 21st), the Yuan held its 86th meeting. The Huang Committee members submitted a report on the reorganized articles, which were approved and immediately skipped the third reading. The full text of the two laws is recorded below:

City Autonomy Law

Chapter 1: Establishment of Cities (Article 1) Cities shall be established in places where people gather and have one or more of the following conditions and may be subordinate to the Executive Yuan: (1) Capital (2) Population of one million or more (3) Special circumstances in politics or economics. If one of the above two or three conditions is met and it is the seat of the provincial government, it shall be subordinate to the provincial government. (Article 2) Cities may be established in places where people gather, the population is 300,000 or more, and industry and commerce are developed, and shall be subordinate to the provincial government. (Article 3) The abolition of a city and the division or change of its area shall be subject to the approval of the National Government. (Article 4) A city is divided into several districts, and the organization within the district is divided into Lü and Lin. Ten households are a Lin, ten Lin are a Lü, and ten or more Lü are a district, but may be changed according to local conditions. (Article 5) In rural areas belonging to a city, if there are special circumstances, they may be organized into townships and towns, and the provisions of the County Autonomy Law regarding townships and towns shall be followed.

Chapter 2: Matters of City Autonomy (Article 6) Matters of city autonomy are as follows: (1) Investigation and registration of households (2) Facilities for childcare, elderly care, poverty alleviation, and disaster relief, and management (3) Grain storage and regulation (4) Labor matters (5) Organization and guidance of cooperatives and mutual aid businesses (6) Customs reform (7) Revitalizing domestic goods (8) Public security and fire protection (9) City finance (10) Management, use, revenue, and disposal of city-owned property (11) Management of city-run enterprises (12) Land administration (13) Public civil engineering and other construction projects (14) Guidance and supervision of citizen building projects (15) Equipment management and supervision and guidance of public utilities (16) Management and supervision of harbors, waterways, docks, warehouses, and ships (17) Education and other cultural matters (18) Preservation of scenic spots and historical sites (19) Public health (20) Other matters belonging to city autonomy.

Chapter 3: City Citizens (Article 7) Citizens of the Republic of China, regardless of gender, who have resided continuously in the city area for more than one year or have a residence for more than two years, are 20 years of age or older, and who have been sworn in and registered are city citizens and have the right to attend the city citizen assembly, the district citizen assembly, and exercise the rights of election, recall, initiative, and referendum. (Article 8) The oath registration in the preceding article shall be held at the district office, and the method shall be determined by the Ministry of Interior. (Article 9) The procedures for city citizens to exercise the four rights of election, recall, initiative, and referendum shall be determined separately.

Chapter 4: City Citizen Assembly (Article 10) The City Citizen Assembly is organized by city citizens and exercises the rights of election, recall, initiative, and referendum. (Article 11) The City Citizen Assembly is held once a year, with meeting places set up in each district on the same day. (Article 12) The City Citizen Assembly is convened by the mayor, and temporary City Citizen Assemblies may be convened when necessary. The City Citizen Assembly or temporary City Citizen Assembly shall be convened by the speaker of the City Council when held for elections or recalls of the mayor or other matters from which the mayor should recuse himself. When a joint request is made by one-twentieth or more of the total number of citizens to the mayor or the speaker of the City Council to convene a temporary City Citizen Assembly, the mayor or the speaker shall convene it immediately. (Article 13) The City Citizen Assembly or temporary City Citizen Assembly shall be valid if one-tenth or more of the total number of citizens are present to vote, and the decision of the majority of the voting citizens shall be valid. The decision in the preceding paragraph shall be announced by the convener.

Chapter 5: City Council (Article 14) A City Council shall be established in the city, organized by city councilors elected by the City Citizen Assembly. (Article 15) The number of city councilors shall be eleven in cities with a population of less than 300,000. For those with a population of more than 300,000, one city councilor shall be added for every 50,000 people, but shall not exceed twenty in total. (Article 16) One-third of the city councilors shall be re-elected each year and may be re-elected consecutively. (Article 17) The powers of the City Council are as follows: (1) Deliberating the city budget and auditing the city final accounts (2) Deliberating city taxes and contracts that increase the city treasury burden (3) Deliberating the operation and disposal of city-owned property (4) Auditing city finances (5) Deliberating city single regulations (6) Recommending municipal reforms to the city government (7) Deliberating matters submitted by the mayor (8) Questioning the mayor (9) Accepting citizen petitions (10) Other powers conferred by law (Article 18) City councilors may not concurrently serve as officials of the city government or its subordinate agencies. (Article 19) City councilors are unpaid, but may be given an allowance for public expenses during meetings. (Article 20) The City Council shall have a speaker and a deputy speaker, each elected by the city councilors using a secret ballot. If the speaker or deputy speaker is vacant due to an accident, a by-election shall be held immediately. (Article 21) When the City Council is in session, the speaker shall preside. If the speaker has an accident, the deputy speaker shall preside. If both the speaker and deputy speaker have accidents, the councilors shall elect one person to be the temporary chairman. (Article 22) The City Council shall hold a regular meeting once every six months, but a temporary meeting shall be convened immediately upon the request of the mayor or one-third or more of the city councilors. The duration of the regular and temporary meetings shall not exceed one month, and all proposals shall be reviewed within the period. (Article 23) The City Council may not convene unless a majority of the councilors are present. The vote on a proposal shall be carried out with the consent of a majority of the councilors present. If the numbers of affirmative and negative votes are equal, the decision shall be made by the chairman. (Article 24) When the City Council is in session, the mayor may be invited to attend the meeting to report or explain. (Article 25) The City Council's resolutions shall be sent to the mayor for execution. If the mayor believes that the resolution is inappropriate, he may send it back for reconsideration with detailed reasons. If two-thirds or more of the councilors still insist on the previous resolution, the mayor shall execute it immediately. If the execution is delayed, the City Council may convene a City Citizen Assembly to decide whether or not to recall the mayor. If the recall motion in the preceding paragraph is rejected by the City Citizen Assembly, all city councilors shall be re-elected immediately. (Article 26) City councilors shall not be held responsible externally for speeches and votes made during meetings. (Article 27) City councilors may not be arrested or detained during sessions without the permission of the City Council, except in the current season. (Article 28) If a city councilor violates the law or neglects his duties, he shall be recalled by the City Citizen Assembly. (Article 29) The City Council shall have a secretary-general and two to seven secretaries to handle records, documents, and accounting affairs under the command of the speaker. The City Council may employ employees during sessions. (Article 30) The rules of procedure of the City Council shall be determined by the City Council. (Unfinished)

The Chao-Shan Region's Native Sugar Suffers Severe Suppression

The Provincial Government Sells National Sugar

Competing with Farmers' Native Sugar

Shantou Dispatch: The Guangdong Provincial Government's National Products Promotion Office, in order to promote its "Five Rams" brand of national sugar, previously used the pretext of revitalizing native sugar to implement sugar industry control, creating numerous difficulties for native sugar from various districts. Recently, the office issued three temporary measures for the transportation and sale of native sugar, suppressing its circulation. All native sugar transportation and sales must be verified by the national products distribution office and a permit obtained before transportation and sale are allowed. This regulation was implemented on the first of this month. The Pu Ning and Chao Yang native associations in Shantou sent a telegram to the provincial government, stating that the National Products Promotion Office's actions were close to destroying national products, requesting its cancellation. The Chaozhou native association in Shanghai also telegraphed Guangdong, stating that the measures for verifying and permitting the transportation and sale of native sugar were intended to prevent the smuggling and adulteration of foreign sugar. However, native sugar is cheap and foreign sugar is expensive, and even the most foolish person would not do this. Moreover, the export of native sugar must be inspected by the Chaozhou Customs, and re-inspected upon arrival at other ports. The procedures are already thorough. Now, suddenly adding attestation procedures during transportation only creates disturbance, without any practical benefit. The native sugar of Chaozhou is purely produced by farmers in rural villages, sparsely manufactured. They toil all year round, working hard, and a family of several depends on this for a living. If the verification procedures are cumbersome, transportation will inevitably be obstructed, turnover will be hampered, and life will become more difficult. At a time when rural villages are bankrupt, this is the only thing they can rely on for survival. Such harsh suppression will immediately lead to cessation of farming and stagnation of commerce. Called protection, it is no different from destruction, forcing us to appeal to your Excellency to order the cancellation of the temporary measures for inspecting native sugar at the factory, etc. According to reports from the Chaoan Nursery and Forestry Commissioner, the Department of Construction had previously ordered investigations in various counties regarding native sugar in the Chaozhou region. Sugarcane planting begins in February in spring and can be harvested by December. For each farming household, the cost of sugarcane seedlings, fertilizer, labor, field rent, land tax, field donations, and expenses for district and township offices, security fees, autonomy fees, harvesting labor, transportation labor, and sugarcane juice extraction fees for sugar mills amounts to 28 silver dollars per acre from planting to sugar boiling. Farmers usually have to borrow from wealthy farmers and sugar merchants to purchase fertilizer and pay public expenses, which are repaid after the sugar is sold or offset with sugar as interest. Farmers organize ancient sugar mills near the farmland, dismantling them immediately after the juice extraction and sugar boiling are completed. The sugar is stored in the farmers' homes. Sugar merchants from Chaozhou and Shantou then send people to the countryside to inspect and purchase the goods. After collection, they are transported to foreign firms in Shantou for packaging and then transshipped to various provinces in the Yangtze River inland for sale. The above is a report from government personnel, showing the hardship of farmers producing sugar.

Currently, the provincial government's measures to suppress native sugar are considered unfeasible in both production and sales, with three points of difficulty: (1) Regardless of the amount of native sugar, when transporting from the inland, a permit must be obtained from the national product public warehouse to accompany the goods, and inspectors must verify the permit along the way to allow passage. (2) When native sugar arrives in Shantou, if it is to be exported, a sample must be wrapped in paper, sealed in a glass bottle, numbered, and submitted to the Bureau of Agriculture and Forestry for chemical verification to see if any foreign sugar impurities have been mixed in. (3) The export of native sugar must have the transportation permit, and the verification permit from the public warehouse before customs can be declared and shipping arranged, with very strict penalties set. After these suppression measures were implemented, farmers all complained bitterly. Moreover, inspectors harass everywhere. The government is clearly aware of this but tacitly approves of it. The National Products Promotion Office's reply to the Chaoan County government's letter serves as the government's defense. The letter states, "The sugar industry control was originally established to revitalize native sugar, plug loopholes, and attempt to save the bankrupt rural economy. Therefore, the control is limited to machine-made white sugar (which does not exist in the Chaozhou region). The privately-operated native yellow sugar can be freely bought and sold in the manufacturing areas, and there is no interference. However, the promotion of sugar from other districts is only subject to procedural inspection to prevent adulteration. There is currently no explicit text on control. However, after investigation, some distributors in nearby districts, in the name of control, create numerous difficulties for the transportation and sale of native sugar, extorting money on pretexts. They collect certificate fees from native sugar retail stores in violation of regulations (i.e., a certain amount of money must be paid for each inspection certificate), causing private sugar merchants and sellers of native sugar to have doubts about manufacturing and sales. Such a situation is no different from assisting the smuggling of foreign sugar and destroying the vitality of native sugar, which is contrary to the government's original intention of developing the provincial sugar industry, and is extremely hateful. Strict prohibition should be enforced to eliminate malpractices." The National Products Promotion Office's words are indeed like this, but there is no evidence that it has actually implemented them.

After investigation, the counties in the Chaozhou region are originally the richest areas for native sugar production. In addition to transporting and selling to various counties in the province, the amount transported annually by sea to various provinces in the Yangtze River for sale is about 2 million dan (each dan is 100 catties). However, it has decreased year by year due to the impact of Javanese white sugar. Since the imposition of taxes on foreign sugar, sugarcane growers in the rural villages of Chaozhou have revived. Each acre of sugarcane garden can produce 4 dan in a good year, and 2-3 dan in a dry year. The market price is 12-13 yuan per dan, and the retail price is 1.5 jiao per catty. However, the strong sales of native sugar pose a major threat to the National Products Promotion Office's "Five Rams" brand national sugar. Therefore, it is resented by the national sugar. As for the national sugar promotion methods, the Second National Sugar Public Warehouse is established in Shantou. Each county purchases from the National Products Promotion Office, ranging from 500 to 2300 packages per month. They must sell the full quota, and more sales get more rebates. Each package weighs 100 catties, with 24th-grade white sugar. The Hong Kong market price is 4.8 yuan per 100 catties. The National Products Promotion Office sells to merchants in Chaozhou and Shantou for 21 yuan in silver dollars, plus 4 jiao for transportation and 5 jiao for inspection. The merchants then hire many inspectors themselves to suppress native sugar. Moreover, the Chaoan distributor sells wholesale for 21.5 yuan per 100 catties in silver dollars. The Chenghai distributor sells the goods exclusively to three merchants in the city, allowing these three merchants to monopolize and raise prices arbitrarily. At the same time, they use the power of inspectors to suppress other native sugar merchants. The above are all public facts, which the National Products Promotion Office has already lamented in its letter. The people can do nothing about it.

The Department of Construction plans to establish a sugar factory in Qu Xi, Jieyang, to purchase sugarcane from the people to make sugar. In the future, there will be a lack of raw materials for native sugar, and farmers will not be able to survive. The situation will inevitably lead to this. Now, new native sugar is about to be on the market. Previously, the Chaoan national sugar distributor could sell 100 packages of national sugar per day. Now, due to the impact of native sugar, it sells less than 60 packages per day on average. Therefore, native sugar is greatly suppressed to support the promotion of national sugar. In fact, the so-called national sugar is a disguised form of foreign sugar, specially operated by the government's National Products Promotion Office, and thus euphemistically called national sugar. Generally, national sugar represents the government's interests, and native sugar represents the interests of rural villages, creating a contradiction. Judging from the current situation of native sugar being suppressed, the demise of native sugar is not far off. It is also regrettable.

[P Songjiang>]

Zhang Xiaohe

Record of the Trial of Suspected Wife Murder

The county court held a criminal hearing this morning (22nd) to try the case of suspected adultery between a brother-in-law and sister-in-law and the murder of the wife east of Huayang Bridge, which caused a sensation throughout the city, and the gallery was full. Zhang Xiaohe, the son of Zhang Xiaoyu, a villager, married Ye Delin's niece on the eighth day of the fourth month through the matchmaker Lu Xianghe. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the thirteenth day of the seventh month, Mrs. Zhang Ye was found dead with more than ten knife wounds. At that time, it was said to be suicide. Later, after the corpse's mother, Ye Lu, and uncle, Ye Delin, investigated based on the statements of fishermen Chen Tutudi and others, they believed that there was a suspicion of adultery between the brother-in-law and sister-in-law and murder. Moreover, when the deceased returned to Ning, she had mentioned the matter of the middle to her mother, which made it even more suspicious. They immediately hired lawyer Wu Chengqi and sued the prosecutor, summoning the defendants Zhang Xiaoyu and sister-in-law Xiao Zhang Shen for interrogation, and based on the testimony of witnesses Chen Tutudi and Xiao Alang, filed a lawsuit with the criminal court. Today, criminal court judge Zhang Yihuang, accompanied by the clerk, ascended the bench, summoned the original defendants and witnesses for interrogation. The defendant hired lawyer Lu Longxiang to defend him. First, the plaintiff Ye Lu and Ye Delin testified about the situation of the accusation, and then the witness Chen Tutudi testified that he was a fisherman. On this day, at dawn, he passed by the Zhang family's door and heard a cry for help, "Mama!" Then he learned of the death of Mrs. Zhang Ye, and the situation of more than ten knife wounds and a severed wrist. The witness Xiao Alang also testified that he had heard arguing the previous day, saying, "What is the reason for uncle sleeping in sister-in-law's room?" The voice was subtle, and then he heard a reply, saying, "Don't you be fierce." Ye Lu also testified that her daughter had told her when she returned to Ning that her brother-in-law and sister-in-law slept in the same room. Yu had sincerely asked her to be patient, and her daughter had left with tears in her eyes. However, when questioned, the defendant vehemently denied the charges. It was already four o'clock in the afternoon, so it was announced that the hearing would be continued on a scheduled date, and the debate was not opened before adjourning. The defendant was returned to custody.

Changshu

The County Organizes a Work Relief Dredging Association

Due to the unusually severe drought this summer, all counties have been affected. Now, the County Construction Association, in order to provide relief to the disaster victims in various counties, held a meeting on the 20th of this month and decided to organize a Work Relief Dredging Association, using work as a form of relief, which is convenient for both public and private interests. The measurement will begin immediately. The resolutions are recorded as follows: (1) For the rivers to be dredged this year, except for the city moat, which will be requisitioned for labor, the dredging of rivers in various villages will be of a work relief nature. (2) Organize a Work Relief Dredging Association to take full responsibility and prepare an outline to be submitted to the department for record. (3) The downstream of the Second Main River, the upstream of the Fourth Main River, and the Lake Cao Pond, Xi Pu and other rivers, have been requested by citizens to be dredged. However, since six places, including Huangsipu, have already been opened for dredging, and funds are insufficient, the scheduled Xuliujing, Meitang, Limutang, Huangsipu, etc., should be measured first. If funds are remaining, a comprehensive plan will be made. (4) There are many places along the river embankment that have collapsed. A letter will be sent to the county to investigate and repair them.

Wuxi

The Weather is Unusually Warm with Little Rain or Snow

In recent months, the weather in the county has been unusually warm with little rain or snow. The Fahrenheit thermometer is often in the range of 55-56 degrees, so seasonal diseases are prevalent, especially diphtheria, which is the most dangerous. After this prolonged drought, the river water is becoming shallower day by day. The river water in the city has a foul smell and cannot be used for drinking, which poses a serious problem for drinking water and fire fighting. The Relief Association Donates Funds to Relieve the Disaster

The county's Relief Association held its first standing committee meeting at the county government yesterday, chaired by County Chief Yan. The matters decided were: 1. The association's donations will be designated for storage in the Farmers' and Chinese Banks. 2. Qin Zhenhua of the relief home was appointed as accountant, Li Baisen of the Chamber of Commerce was appointed as general affairs officer, and Zhou Shaoji of the county government was appointed as document officer, responsible for handling association affairs. 3. The donation register will be numbered and lightly managed by Li Baisen. 4. The donation register will be distributed to the fundraising groups for fundraising. 5. The remaining funds from the county's flood relief association will be transferred to the association by the county government through a letter to the county property management office, specifically for relief purposes. The county government will also be requested to allocate the funds for repairing embankments in various districts to the association for relief purposes.

Yinjiang

Huangtiangang Will Begin Dredging This Year

The dredging of Huangtiangang outside the North Gate had been previously ordered by the Department of Construction to be remeasured and redrawn by the county for submission to the department. The head of the third division, Cui Hualiang, was sent to the province to personally explain to Director Shen and discuss dredging methods. It was decided to start construction before the end of the year. The estimated cost is 70,000 yuan, which will be covered by funds raised locally. If it is not enough, the province will subsidize it. The second phase of the project will be carried out this year to do the earthwork, and the ship lock will be built next spring.

Changzhou

The Yun Village Police Station Seizes a Large Quantity of Poison Pills

Huang Yuncheng, a patrol officer of the 7th Sub-Station directly under the Wu Yi Yun Village Public Security Bureau, dispatched patrol captain Li Weizhang to lead patrol officers to patrol the town at about 7 pm on the 20th. While patrolling on the west side of the motor road, they saw a small boat in the Jiangshanbang River traveling rapidly from east to west. Suspecting that it was suspicious, they ordered it to stop for inspection. Unexpectedly, the boat ignored the order and rowed quickly, still attempting to escape. They immediately led the police to chase after it. They saw a person on the boat suddenly jump into the water to escape, and another person threw a large package into the river. The patrolman Li Yucheng jumped into the river to swim and chase after the person, and quickly captured him. He was taken ashore and interrogated, and he gave his name as Xu Yaoshu. The person on the boat was his father, named Shunrong. One hundred iles of poison pills were found on his body. At this time, the small boat and the boatman Xu Shunfa were also captured, and a large package of poison pills was retrieved from the river, containing 30 packages, totaling about 30,000 pills, all soaked in water. They were immediately taken to the station together. After a preliminary interrogation, on the 21st, a document was prepared and police were dispatched to escort them to the city public security bureau for interrogation.

Zhenjiang

Most of the Provincial Warehouse is Completed

The Jiangsu Department of Finance, in view of the current situation of rural bankruptcy and disaster, believes that the construction of grain storage warehouses is an important task. Previously, the provincial government had decided to build large-scale provincial warehouses in ten grain-producing counties, including Wu County (the main stored items are rice and wheat, supplemented by silk cocoons and straw mats), Taixian (mainly rice, beans, and wheat), Yancheng (rice, beans, and cotton), Xuzhou (wheat, beans, hemp, and peanuts), Yixing (rice, wheat, and cocoons), Wujiang (rice, cocoons, and leaves), Rugao (wheat, cotton, and peanuts), and Changshu (mainly rice). The construction of the remaining two counties, Suqian and Huaiyin, was later and due to the gradually colder weather, the progress of the project was somewhat hindered. Therefore, the Department of Finance decided to start construction again next spring when the weather is warmer.

Haimen

The Shanghai Telephone Line is Scheduled for Connection

The county's long-distance telephone was originally privately operated. This spring, the Ministry of Communications ordered the county's telegraph bureau to take over the management and connect calls with various counties north of the Yangtze River. Now, stores in the county and city feel that it is very inconvenient that Haimen is only separated from Shanghai by a river and cannot be connected. Moreover, Nantong was connected to Shanghai in August of this year, and the transmission of news is quite efficient. Therefore, they jointly submitted a petition to the county chamber of commerce, which forwarded a letter to the bureau requesting that it find a way to connect the line. The bureau chief, Huang Binglin, prepared a plan and submitted it to the Land Administration Bureau for review. Yesterday, the bureau sent a telegram approving the matter and setting a deadline to start connecting the line in January next year.

Jiaxing

The Farmers' Bank Recovers Overdue Payments

The Jiaxing County Farmers' Bank is currently pursuing overdue payments from various cooperatives. It had previously proposed a method of reducing interest rates and setting a deadline for repayment. Then, it sent personnel to the various indebted cooperatives and guarantors to agree on a repayment period. Now that the deadline for recovery has expired, a small number of cooperatives, disregarding their credit, have still not repaid, and some are procrastinating. The bank believes that if it does not pursue the payments strictly, it will have a significant impact on future development. Therefore, it has specially prepared a list of the amount of debt owed by each cooperative along with the names of the guarantors, preparing to file a lawsuit according to law. It has also submitted a request to the Departments of Finance and Construction to order the county to pursue the payments.

Tianjin

The Zhanghua Branch Officially Opens

The Shanghai Zhanghua Woolen Textile Company previously sent factory manager Wu Bokang to Tianjin to prepare for the establishment of the Tianjin branch and test the machines for production. Everything is now ready, and the official opening is scheduled for December 6th. Invitations were sent to all sectors of society to visit. The newly appointed mayor, Zhang Ting'e, and people from all walks of life went to visit and were very satisfied with the excellent management.

Local News

Wang Chonghui Met with Sun Ke Yesterday

Reporting on the Hong Kong Trip and Exchanging Opinions

Sun Discussed that Mr. Hu Can Come North After the Spring Warms Up

Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning, accompanied by Legislative Yuan member Fu Bingchang and others. Central Committee member Dr. Wang Chonghui went to Sun's residence at about 9:00 am yesterday morning to meet with him. Mr. Wang departed for Zhejiang at 5:00 pm yesterday, accompanied by Chen Shaokuan, Zhou Xiangxian, and others. Details are as follows:

Sun and Wang Meeting: President Sun came to Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning because the Legislative Yuan announced a two-week recess. Mr. Wang Chonghui, who had just returned to Shanghai from the south, drove to Sun's residence from the World Academy at about 9:00 am to meet with him. The two talked for an hour. Mr. Wang reported in detail on his two meetings with Mr. Hu Zhantang in Hong Kong and left at 10:00 am. Mr. Sun decided to stay in Shanghai for a rest because the Legislative Yuan was in recess for two weeks. During this period, he will handle matters related to the Sun Yat-sen Culture and Education Hall.

Sun's Talk: After Mr. Wang left, President Sun received reporters at his residence. According to his talk, Mr. Wang Liangchou came to visit to report on his two meetings with Mr. Hu in Hong Kong. Before the Fifth Plenary Session, I went south to visit Mr. Hu with Mr. Wang. At that time, because the meeting was about to be held, I could not stay long and returned north first, leaving Mr. Wang in Hong Kong to continue talks with Mr. Hu and others. According to Mr. Wang, the result of the continued talks was even better. It is no longer a problem for Mr. Hu Zhantang to leave Hong Kong and come north. Mr. Hu originally planned to come to Shanghai immediately, but because the climate in Shanghai is colder than in Hong Kong, and Mr. Hu is weak, he plans to depart when the spring warms up. When Mr. Hu comes, it is feared that Mr. Chen Jitang and others will not be able to come north with him, because Mr. Chen has important local responsibilities and cannot leave his post for a long time. As for the national solidarity, the future is even more optimistic. During this period of national crisis, only national unity can save the nation and survive. All comrades in the southwest have expressed their sincerity and will work with the central government. As for the three points mentioned by Wang Liangchou in today's newspaper, they are all things that the central government should do. The so-called cooperation method is a plan on how to actively proceed in the future, and is not a condition. The southwest and the central government have long been cooperating. The Guangdong Provincial Finance Director Qu Fangpu went to Nanjing to visit President Wang to discuss the suppression of remaining bandits in Guangdong, Guangxi, and Yunnan provinces.

Wang's Talk: Wang Chonghui told reporters yesterday morning that he had met with President Wang, Minister Kong, President Sun, and others to report on his trip to Hong Kong and exchange opinions. The results were very good, and the prospects for cooperation are very optimistic. As for President Sun's intention, he believes that the southwestern propositions are all principles, and further actions should be taken in the future.

Departing for Zhejiang Yesterday: At 2:30 pm yesterday, Guangdong Finance Director Qu Fangpu specially went to the World Academy to visit Mr. Wang, and left after talking until about 3:00 pm. Mr. Wang, accompanied by Wei Daoming, departed for Zhejiang at 5:00 pm yesterday. Those traveling with him included Navy Minister Chen Shaokuan, Hangzhou Mayor Zhou Xiangxian, and Song Zi'an. It is said that Mr. Wang will return to Shanghai in two or three days and go to The Hague to return to his post at the beginning of next month.

A Celebration Will Be Held at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

All Cinemas in the City Will Be Open in the Morning

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Fourth New Ship, Hai Zhen, Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

The Supervising Engineer, Mr. Shi Gan, Arrived on the Ship

Hai Li Was Officially Received Yesterday, and Invitations for Scheduled Visits Were Sent Out

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's fourth new ship, Hai Zhen, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. The Hai Li was officially received by the company. Visits for people from all walks of life are scheduled for Monday. Details are as follows:

Hai Zhen Arrives in Shanghai: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's fourth new ship, Hai Zhen, sailed to Shanghai after its completion in England. At 2 PM on the 21st, the ship arrived at the Tongsha waters outside Wusong. The Shanghai Moller & Company obtained permission from China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to send a pilot to the mouth of Song to guide the ship to Shanghai. It was originally scheduled to enter the port at 4 PM that afternoon, but due to fog on the sea, it anchored in Wusong at that time. It was not until the fog cleared yesterday morning that it was guided into the port and sent to the Jiangnan Shipyard, where it will be painted and the hull inspected before official acceptance.

Appointment of Captain: Mr. Shi Gan, the supervising engineer sent by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to England to oversee the construction of the four ships, has returned to Shanghai with the Hai Zhen, as all four ships have been completed. He arrived at the company yesterday and reported everything to Mr. Liu Hongsheng. The company has decided to appoint Mr. Dax, former captain of the Pu An ship, as the captain of the Hai Zhen. The first and second mates, as well as the chief engineer, have also been internally determined and will be announced next Monday. The ship is scheduled to begin receiving all deck departments from the 25th.

Reception of Hai Li: The third new ship, Hai Li, has completed its inspection at the Jiangnan Shipyard. Captain Xi Shibia and First Mate Chen Bangda were appointed to the ship yesterday. Yesterday, the company assigned Zhao Yuntai, director of the Shipping Department, and Shen Jiyun, chief captain, to the ship for official acceptance. Hai Li was handed over by Moller & Company, representing the shipyard, and the company flag and national flag were immediately hoisted. It is now scheduled to sail to the Jinliyuan Wharf today. Yesterday afternoon, the company telegraphed the Ministry of Communications, stating that the Hai Li was officially received today (the 22nd) and reporting the matter.

Additional Invitation to Visit: Labor union, the Captains' Association, and other leaders of party and government institutions, such as Yang Hu, did not participate in the previous invitation to visit the Hai Yuan. Therefore, the company specially issued an additional 50 invitations and prepared refreshments and meals for 50 guests on the Hai Li, inviting leaders from the Party and government institutions to visit the ship at the Jinliyuan Wharf on Monday morning. Liu Hongsheng will personally board the ship to receive the guests. The ship will be scheduled to sail to Nanhua. Because the Hai Li has a Chinese captain, it will also give up Hong Kong passengers.

Jiangzhe Silk Industry Short-Term Public Bonds Drawn Yesterday Morning for Redemption

Six Bonds Drawn, Totaling 180,000 Yuan in Principal and Interest

Payment Will Be Made by Six Banks, Including the Central Bank, at the End of the Month

The ninth lottery drawing for redemption of the Jiangzhe Silk Industry Short-Term Public Bonds of the Republic of China, Year 21, was held at 10:00 AM yesterday in the main hall of the Banking Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road. More than ten representatives from various sectors attended. Mr. Qin Runqing presided over the event. Six bonds were drawn, totaling 180,000 yuan in principal and interest. All winning bonds will be paid out in cash by the main banks, including the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, National Goods Bank, Jiangsu Bank, and Hangzhou Zhejiang Local Bank, starting at the end of this month. Details are as follows:

Representatives in Attendance: Qin Runqing, Chairman of the Jiangzhe Silk Industry Short-Term Public Bonds Fund Management Committee; Shen Zaochi of the Auditing Department; Chen Lin and Wang Fangsheng of the Zhejiang Provincial Government; Jin Wenyuan of the Central Bank; Han Tiaoqing of the Bank of China; Mao Shijian of the Bank of Communications; Xu Boming and Yang Chengyi of the Jiangsu Bank; Pan Yonghe of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank; Song Xunlun of the Zhejiang Local Bank; and more than ten other representatives.

Chairman's Report: After the ceremonial procedures, Chairman Qin Runqing reported, "Today is the date of the ninth drawing for redemption of the Jiangzhe Silk Industry Short-Term Public Bonds of the Republic of China, Year 21. I am pleased to have you all here to supervise and observe. The total value of the bonds issued is 3 million yuan. This is the ninth drawing, and a total of six bonds will be drawn, totaling 180,000 yuan in principal and interest. All winning bonds will be paid out in cash by the six banks: Central, China, Communications, National Goods, Jiangsu, and Hangzhou Zhejiang Local Bank starting on the 31st of this month. Now, I request the supervisors to verify the bond stubs and the bond stub register in preparation for the drawing."

Winning Numbers: After the Chairman's report, the supervisors verified the bond stubs and the bond stub register. The lottery drawing was then conducted, and six bonds were drawn: "No. 14," "No. 23," "No. 31," "No. 44," "No. 63," and "No. 81." All winning numbers will be posted publicly and announced in the newspaper by the association.

Private Postal Services in Panic as Deadline Approaches

Held Reception Last Night to Issue Declaration

But Post Office Claims There Will Be No Impediment to Their Livelihoods

Hua Yunjin, the general representative of private postal services nationwide, Yin Yuantong, and others held a banquet last night to entertain public organizations and the press in this city to report on the Ministry of Communications' order to cease operations. At the same time, they issued a declaration. However, the post office claimed that if the private postal services cease operations but do not violate postal regulations, there is still a way to maintain their livelihoods. Details are as follows:

Reception for Various Sectors: At 6 PM yesterday, the industry specially held a reception at the Tai He Yuan Restaurant on Second Ma Road to entertain public organizations and the press in this city. Attendees included Yu Zuoting, chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Yu Qiaqing, a leader in the business community; representatives from the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, Ningbo Association, Farmers' Association, Education Association, and other organizations; and more than 50 reporters from various newspapers. Hua Yunjin and Yin Yuantong, two representatives, made announcements. The banquet lasted until after 9 PM and ended in a cheerful atmosphere.

Declaration Issued: The industry issued a declaration stating, "Our private postal service industry originated during the Jiaqing period of the Qing Dynasty. It has always been known for its prompt service and reliable integrity, and has therefore been deeply appreciated by all sectors. When the postal service was first established on a trial basis at the end of the Guangxu period, it was only limited to major cities and towns. At that time, although people submitted their letters to the post office for delivery, silver, clothing, and other items were still sent through the private postal services. This is a history of hundreds of years. Not only is it convenient and reassuring, but the prosperity of commerce and the stability of society are particularly evident in the past achievements. After the Republic of China, the postal service was established as a state-owned enterprise, and the authorities actively made reforms. However, letters and other items only reached important towns, and remittances and packages only reached cities, and the cumbersome procedures made rural people flinch. Therefore, before the national postal service can be fully established nationwide, private postal services still have value in existence. Now, the postal authorities, seeking to take credit, only know how to unify postal rights and do not understand the needs of society. They hastily submitted a proposal for suppression. The Ministry of Communications has issued a notice limiting the nationwide private postal services to cease operations by the end of Year 23. But once implemented, it will cause great suffering to our compatriots in remote rural areas who live abroad. For example, those who do business in cities and commercial ports, whose monthly income is not abundant and who rely on it to support their families, but whose homes are in rural areas far from the city, have always relied on the private postal services to deliver money to them on a monthly basis. If they switch to the postal service, they must go to the general office to send and receive, and they must find a reliable guarantor, which is cumbersome. The ignorant villagers will be helpless, and the expensive postage will increase the burden, which is not the blessing of the common people. The unemployment of all our industry employees is another matter. In view of this, our industry has tried its best to argue and petition various central agencies to allow for a delay in the closure, and at the same time, to seek a satisfactory solution for the aftermath. The resulting images are still satisfactory, but it also depends on the support of our colleagues to achieve success. We have always admired the leaders of your association for their insight into public opinion and their deep understanding of social needs. We dare to ask for unanimous support to request the central competent department to consider social needs and take into account the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of employees in the private postal service industry, and to allow a suspension of the implementation and a delay in the closure before a satisfactory solution for the aftermath is found. Society will be fortunate, and our industry will be fortunate."

Post Office's Statement: After the Ministry of Communications issued an order limiting all private postal services to cease operations by the end of this year, the Shanghai Private Postal Service Association convened a meeting of representatives from private postal services in various provinces, and went to the Party and government agencies in this city to petition for the transfer of the request to the Ministry of Communications to withdraw the order. On the 14th of this month, representatives Yin Yuantong, etc., were appointed to go to Beijing and jointly petition the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Communications with representatives from various provinces to request the maintenance of the status quo. After returning to Shanghai, they convened a meeting at the Southern City Private Postal Service Association to report on the petition process. Because the deadline is approaching, a reporter from the New Voice News went to the Shanghai office of the General Post Office on North Sichuan Road to inquire. The person in charge of the office said, "In Year 17 of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Communications held a communications conference and resolved that all private postal services should be abolished by Year 19. Later, because the industry merchants repeatedly requested, the Ministry of Communications, out of consideration, specially approved a flexible solution and separately formulated five provisional measures for private postal services to register and obtain licenses, so that each private postal service could register, obtain a license, and continue to operate in accordance with the regulations, giving the industry merchants an opportunity to gradually close and change industries. Later, in response to the request of the industry in various places, the Ministry of Communications again extended the registration period by one year. This is enough to show the authorities' repeated tolerance and consideration for the industry, and their concern for both sides. Moreover, after the General Post Office received the ministry's order limiting all private postal services to cease operations by the end of this year, at the beginning of the year, it ordered each district post office administration to notify each private postal service to prepare to gradually cease operations. According to the reports submitted by each of these administrations, many private postal services in various places are preparing to cease operations, and 23 have already voluntarily ceased operations. Yesterday, another report was received from the Shanghai Administration, stating that the district has already ceased operations, with a total of seven companies including the previous ones. Private postal services that have not registered are violating postal regulations and have long been subject to suppression. As for the private postal services, they can still make use of their original credibility, change their names, and deliver items and money to the people. This does not conflict with postal regulations and can solve the livelihood problems of the industry merchants."

Shao Lizi Returned to His Hometown Yesterday

Will Return to Shaanxi to Take Office at the End of This Month

Shaanxi Provincial Government Chairman Shao Lizi took advantage of his attendance at the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Committee to come to Shanghai from Beijing to discuss investment and development in the Northwest with the banking community in this city. Grand Memorial Service for Mr. Shi Liangcai by Over Eighty Public Organizations in This City

Today, at 2:00 PM, held at the City Chamber of Commerce...

...Presided over by Mayor Wu Yu-tsoting and others...

The late Mr. Shi Liangcai, Speaker of the Shanghai Municipal Council and member of the China Society, dedicated himself to social and cultural undertakings for nearly forty years, enjoying widespread respect throughout the country. Unfortunately, on the 13th of last month, while returning to Shanghai from Hangzhou, he was suddenly assassinated and died. The shocking news spread, causing deep sorrow. Therefore, the Shanghai Municipal Government, Municipal Council, Local Coordination Council, Daily Newspaper Association, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, Universal Student Association of China, and others initiated preparations for a memorial service to express their condolences. Various public organizations in the city actively participated, reaching over eighty. Now that the preparatory office has completed the preparations, the memorial service will be held at 2:00 PM this afternoon in the Grand Hall of the City Chamber of Commerce at Tianhou Palace Bridge, North Henan Road.
