Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Random Talks

Smiles May Not Always Be Frequent

— Xu Zhi

Everyone says this year is the year of magazines, but I would rather say: at the same time, this year is also the "year of essays," the "year of humor." In fact, the number of publications dedicated to "humorous essays" published this year is indeed particularly large: the original "The Analects" need not be mentioned, as it is the pioneer in specializing in "humor." The subsequent "Ren Jian Shi," "Hua An," "Hua Mei," etc., are also well-known for their "humor" this year. At the same time, many large magazines also had to specially publish "humorous" essays because they saw the prevalence of the "humor" trend. As for the essays prevalent this year, in my opinion, they were also derived from this "humor" trend. Not to mention anything else, just the book title "Selection of Excellent Essays" is already "humorous" enough. Thus, under everyone saying "this year is the year of magazines," saying again that this year is the "year of humor," and therefore saying that 1934 is the "era of humor," who can say that is wrong?

The word "humor" is originally a transliteration of the word "Humour." Because this year, the trend of "humor" is prevalent in our country, people can see or hear people talking about "humor" in magazines, in general newspaper butt, at banquets, and even on the streets. Therefore, what is the meaning of these two words "humor"? What should the English word Humour be translated into Chinese? This has become a problem. Some people say that the word Humour should still be translated as "humor," while others say it should be translated as "humiao." Someone even advocated translating it as "yumo," and the magazine "Huamei" even used the discussion of this issue as its inaugural message, saying that it was to avoid the problem of "phonetic loan," and advocated using "yumiao." From this, it can be imagined how much people are paying attention to "humor."

However, where does the strength of "humorous" articles lie? Professor Liang Shiqiu said: We don't look at advertisements, we look at the quality of the goods. Now, let's just randomly list some "humorous" essays to take a look丨丨

(1) "When I was a child, I studied in a church school, where foreigners directly taught English from the first grade of elementary school. Therefore, sometimes elementary school students cannot directly express their meaning in English. Once, in a foreign lady's English class, an elementary school student urgently needed to urinate and wanted to go to the toilet, so he pointed to his crotch and said to the foreign lady: Waterwillconeouthere (Water is going to come out from here)."

(2) "A young man and woman said to a modern girl: "I love you very much!"

That modern girl replied, "I know, I love you very much too!"

"Then, don't you love others?"

"What if I love others?"

"Then I must shoot the person you love to death with a pistol!"

"Then you better prepare two machine guns!"'"

(3) "The writer Bai Wei quarreled with Yang Sao, so angry that she said bitterly:

"I must kill you!"

"It's good if you can kill me." Yang Sao walked up to Bai Wei with a stubborn head and said this.

"Am I still keeping you?" So Bai Wei took a pair of scissors and cut off a few strands of Yang Sao's hair."

We have only looked at these few "goods" and already feel they are "humorous" enough, but besides making people happy and laugh, what other meaning do these things have? Even if there are also satirical texts in them, but because they have no theory as a backing, we still can't get anything besides feeling happy after reading them. The impression it gives us is still very vague.

I believe that the general readers of China have already learned a valuable lesson in several major movements: they know the importance of theory (as for what kind of theory is needed, that is of course another question); moreover, with the development of the Chinese cultural movement, the general readers' level of knowledge is higher, so what they require is not just more profound and systematic theories. After this year's "humor" trend, after trying out general essays, their demand for systematic and profound theories is even more urgent. I can say that the general readers now buy a book or a magazine not just casually for entertainment, their purpose must be to explore profound theories; they read an article because they want to gain profound knowledge about a certain issue, not just casually flipping through it. Therefore, I believe that the "humorous" essays and even general essays that are prevalent this year will no longer be able to maintain their superior position. If you don't believe it, then look at the Chinese publishing industry in 1935, and see whether publications dedicated to "humorous essays" are most popular with general readers, or whether "Sun Yat-sen Culture and Education Hall Quarterly," "Newcomer," "World Knowledge," "The Great Wall," "Women's Voice"... are most popular with readers?

Sunday Literary Society

Imagination, Life, and Literary Works

— Zi

Without a real society, there would naturally be no literary works: literary works are a form of life depicted by writers, arising from the real society. However, a writer's depiction of reality is not like a photographer's photography, simply and rigidly copying things as they are; their depiction of reality must pass through their complex minds and be finely and artistically depicted. In this process, "imagination" is essential. In fact, the works of general romanticists naturally carry strong colors of imagination; even the works of naturalists who use positivism as their method of creation, in a sense, are depicted through their imagination. Everyone knows that Flaubert was a naturalist writer, but even in his creative process, he had to find a unique noun to represent a thing in his mind, and a unique adjective to describe the characteristics of that thing; if he did not quietly ponder and imagine, how could he achieve his wish? Zola was even a naturalist who had reached the pinnacle. His attitude towards creation was almost like that of a scientist. He first had to collect materials, personally go to live among the characters he wanted to describe, to interview those women who are related to his creation, then to realistically depict the things he wanted to depict: this seems to have no element of imagination, but can you say that his "Rougon-Macquart" series, such a massive novel, its story structure, the expression of its various characters, the arrangement of its various scenes, the organization of its words and sentences, did not pass through his imagination? Of course, one cannot say that 丨丨丨From this, it can be seen that the element of imagination in literary works is an undeniable fact.

However, the so-called "imagination" is not an empty fabrication by the writer, but is carried out under his life experience. No matter how good a writer is at "imagining," he cannot imagine thoughts and situations that absolutely do not exist in the world, nor can he imagine things that have nothing to do with his social life. The author of "Journey to the West" said that Sun Wukong could somersault one hundred and eight thousand miles, which is of course a fantastic "imagination," but if there was no such thing as "somersaulting" in the world, and there were no numbers like "one hundred and eight thousand miles," could he still "imagine" like this? To go deeper, if Chinese society did not have strange monster ideas, and there were no people whose real lives were empty and wanted to find a world of fantasy, could the author of "Journey to the West" rely solely on his imagination to create such a mythical novel?

Throughout history, many literary theorists have made the "element of imagination" in literature very mysterious, believing that literary works are entirely produced by the writer's imagination. The British Coleridge even wrote a large "Theory of Imagination," arguing that the reason why literary works can move people lies entirely in their imaginative elements; even the more progressive literary theorist Ruskin said that poetry is "the noble basis for implying noble emotions with the power of imagination." In this way, it is no wonder that our literary theorists "value imagination" and separate it from life experience!

If we want to talk about "valuing imagination" and mystifying it, then we have to introduce the aesthetes. Oscar Wilde, in his "The Decay of Lying," besides saying that "lying" is "beautiful and not practical stories," even fiercely attacked the naturalist Zola, saying: "From an artistic point of view, Zola's works are almost without value, only zero points... Our requirements for art are rarity, charm, and imagination, simply put, just beauty. The so-called truly existing person is the meaning of a person who has never existed in this real world. Therefore, when writers borrow characters from the real world, they should at least not use sketches of real-world characters, but should transform these characters. But Zola's characters are all sketches. His works have no value precisely because of this reason." This is truly extremely mysterious! In fact, Wilde and his aestheticism are also a product of British social life at the end of the nineteenth century. If there were no decadent lives of enjoyment for British citizens and many parasitic classes in the nineteenth century, there would be no many "fabricated" literary works and aestheticism of Wilde. Wilde's life of enjoyment, aesthetic art, and all his mysterious imaginations were possessed by the new citizens and many parasitic classes of Britain at that time. Wilde was just reflecting them in literature and even in his personal life丨

In short, writers need and must imagine when creating, but this is not an empty fantasy separated from their social life, but is carried out on the basis of their life experience and knowledge; even those writers who indulge in fantasy, their works are a reflection of their social life, and are by no means products of empty imagination. As for some writers who do not describe real things, but go to pursue an empty ideal world beyond reality, the reason is that his social life stipulates that he cannot or dare not face reality, so that he has to resort to pure imagination when creating; at the same time, there are also some writers who try hard to describe reality, but the result is either distorting reality or failing to fully express reality, becoming an empty thing, the reason for this is also that under the regulation of their social life, they cannot correctly understand reality and fully express reality. Therefore, a writer must bravely approach real life, must correctly understand reality, must have rich experience and knowledge of social life, and of course must also have artistic expression talent, then his imagination, his subjective consciousness, and his descriptive laws can conform to the state and requirements of objective things, and thus can create great works. Everyone knows that Turgenev once portrayed a nihilist Bazarov, "and Artsibashev also gave himself the same sociological and aesthetic task as Turgenev," portraying a Sanin, but fair critics all said that Bazarov was a real character, and Sanin was a "constructed" character, so Artsibashev's description was a failure, so what is the reason for this? I think this can only be explained in their social life (including artistic talent and their ability to recognize reality): the former can correctly recognize reality and express the spirit of the times, while the latter cannot.

Life

Effective Learning Laws Based on Psychological Insights

— Yu

I have never seen a person with mediocre knowledge create an extraordinary career. So, where does knowledge come from? I think that besides "learning," there is probably no other better way.

In today's world, everything must be "scientific," economical and effective, in order to defeat others. The attitude towards learning is the same. We must never again be like the ancient scholars who "buried themselves for ten years" in order to seek "divine enlightenment," because that kind of learning attitude is okay for the leisure class to spend their leisure time, but in today's people who generally pay attention to time economy, it is impossible to take such a circuitous path.

Five years ago, my teacher Dr. Huang Jingsi once orally translated Whipple's "How to Study" thirty-eight articles on the podium. The meaning is profound and is an effective learning law with psychological insights. I think that for a person who is struggling with how to learn, this can very well be his motto. These thirty effective learning laws are: 1. Maintain physical health. 2. Pay attention to and remedy physical defects. 3. Create an "environment" suitable for learning. 4. Develop the habit of learning in one place. 5. Learning must have a certain time. 6. The next lesson should have a considerable preparation after this lesson. 7. Start working. 9. Concentrate! 10. Do not overwork or worry. 11. Work with the purpose of learning and remembering. 12. Learning must have "motivation." 13. Remove the idea of learning for the teacher. 14. Never be easy to ask people unless it is absolutely necessary. 15. The "purpose" must be fully understood. 16. To get new knowledge, you must review old knowledge. 17. When previewing, first glimpse its outline. 18. If you encounter multiple types of work with different degrees of difficulty, you can do the difficult or easy ones first according to your past experience or ideals. 19. The learned movements must be suitable for future applications (such as the order of strokes, muscle movements during practice, which are very easy to form habits). 20. Learn important work for permanent use. 21. Pay attention to and remedy your shortcomings. 22. The daily lessons must be selected for their importance for judgment or criticism. 23. Secondary lessons or knowledge do not need to spend too much time to memorize them. 24. Learning time should not be too short or too long. 25. Lessons that need to be practiced should be practiced in stages. Concentrated practice is not very efficient. 26. Work must be stopped at a considerable time and a sign must be left. 17. After hard work, there must be a considerable rest time. 28. Use various methods to concentrate your thoughts. 29. Develop the habit of giving examples for "principles." 30. Develop the habit of psychological review. 31. If necessary, you can add comments to the book. 32. If the learning materials are many and difficult, you can make an "outline" for easy memorization. 33. Apply the knowledge you have gained when working. 34. You must memorize the definitions, formulas, dates, and outlines of professional terms (once you have to memorize them strongly, and you must understand them). 35. When the memorized materials are difficult to remember, you have to think of various mechanical methods to memorize them. 36. When reading poetry and speeches, do not divide them into paragraphs. 37. Reading aloud and reciting quickly are easy to remember. 38. Do not take too many notes in class, but you must develop the habit of organizing notes.

Page 22

Elementary School Teachers

— Yin Qu

The importance of elementary school education in the entire process of education is known and can be expressed by almost everyone. However, the lives of the elementary school teachers who implement this education are like pitiful withered grass, growing in the damp corners of the wall, without sunlight, without rain, and it seems that heaven and earth let it grow naturally and let it perish naturally, without attracting anyone's attention.

Although, in the entire elementary school education circle, there are also a few who receive higher treatment, but after all, among millions of elementary school teachers, they only account for the smallest number of the smallest number. At the same time, even in Shanghai, except for municipal, Public Works Bureau-established, and a few private schools, the lives of most elementary school teachers are not more reasonable than those of elementary school teachers in poor rural areas.

The lives of most elementary school teachers are below the horizontal line丨

For example, taking a city only thirty kilometers away from Shanghai as an example, the elementary school education there has made considerable progress in both form and spirit in recent years, and is praised by many educators who have visited there. However, the salaries of the teachers are still so low! The standard of treatment is based on the standard of each person's academic qualifications: such as twenty-six yuan for graduates of high school normal schools, twenty-four yuan for high school graduates, and twenty-two yuan for graduates of rural teachers' schools. Although this standard of treatment is slightly more than the number of only eight yuan in a certain county in Jiangbei, if the six yuan for food is deducted, only a dozen yuan are left. And it is very obvious that this standard of treatment does not take the true teaching efficiency as the basis, but only pays attention to the titles in vain (for example, rural teachers with four-year professional training receive less treatment than old-system high school graduates without professional training). As a result, those teachers who are truly dedicated to education are forced to swallow their anger and are filled with resentment.

Moreover, a certain city is close to Shanghai. In the adjacent areas, often a town has a municipal elementary school and a county elementary school. Only a few steps apart, their treatments are completely different (note: the lowest treatment for elementary schools in Shanghai rural areas is thirty-five yuan, and more to one hundred yuan). This spiritually puts most elementary school teachers in a decadent and unmotivated situation, but in the final analysis, this is because China's education does not have a complete plan, so how can we bear to blame elementary school teachers deeply?

I once heard an elementary school teacher sigh and say: "Our generation, relying on the remaining legacy of our fathers and brothers, can still receive secondary education; but what about our next generation? What will we fathers take to educate and cultivate them?" This kind of feeling about one's own life is probably spreading in the elementary school education circle.

In addition to salary, there is no talk of "security." The term of employment for teachers is still half a year, so most people have the mentality of "five days in the capital." At the end of a semester, the turnover of teachers is as frequent as on the political stage, which is a considerable waste of teaching and training. Other things, such as preferential treatment for female teachers during childbirth and the regulations for pension funds, are also out of the question.

Under such treatment, their work cannot be made any easier. Every day from morning to dusk, in addition to the one thousand and several hundred minutes of class work per week, they also have to spend more time managing children, correcting test papers, and filling out tables and books in school administrative affairs. When children's homework or sports competitions are held, the teachers even hate not being able to work day and night to guide the work, because although the competition is for children, the test results belong to the teachers' reputation and future. Other things, such as exhibitions, etc., are nominally for students, but in fact, they are nothing more than adding many unexpected tasks to the teachers in addition to the hard routine work. In short, their lives are busy, busy, and the third one is still busy! If we add the aforementioned poverty, then the lives of elementary school teachers are intertwined with poverty and busyness.

The so-called education experts who live in foreign-style houses say repeatedly; "Elementary school education is a noble career, elementary school education is a noble career丨" However, the injection of this anesthetic has absolutely no effect. The "Jiaxing woman Zhang Yuzhen, who once served as an elementary school teacher and acting principal, was induced to Shanghai by her fellow villager and girlfriend Zhuang Suzhen, who worked as a female receptionist at Wing On Company in Shanghai, because her salary was meager, resulting in a tragic violation" reported by various newspapers on December 15 last year reflects the general elementary school teachers currently in office cannot be content with their noble career status, and are eagerly seeking a solution to their livelihood.

The tide of the times is moving forward non-stop. Those who serve as elementary school teachers, because their work is too busy and the material environment of economic conditions is bound, they have very few opportunities for further study. After leaving school for only a few years, they have already been far away from the air of new ideas and are slowly declining, declining!

"Elementary school teachers are selling their youth," elementary school teachers often painfully gnaw at this sentence.

A few miles away from my hometown, there is an elementary school. The former principal is now serving as the school's janitor. Although he could not grasp the times and follow the trend, resulting in his own doom, it is also a major tragedy in the world.

All of this is developed abnormally under the economic conditions. The more we say that elementary school education is important, the more urgently the treatment of elementary school teachers needs to be improved, but I wonder if our education experts have ever paid attention to this in their dreams!

Overseas Correspondence Team

A Glimpse of the Western Front Black Mermaid

— Yang Xiaocheng

Report from Genoa, Italy

Speaking of the words "Western Front," everyone will immediately think of the world-famous novel "All Quiet on the Western Front" and its movie, right? Although I use these two words as the title with the suspicion of being the same, I use our hometown Shanghai as the center of departure, so that distinguishing eastward to Japan or the United States as the eastward route, and westward to Europe as the westward route is the title. I have now completed the voyage to Western Europe and arrived in Italy.

It is really impossible for a traveler lying in a ship to describe the political and economic conditions of the countries or commercial ports he has passed through, because a superficial browsing cannot fully understand the depths of their social conditions. The only thing that can provide me with communication materials is the "Black Mermaid" that I saw with my own eyes during the journey.

The term "mermaid" is very loud in China, but I am now going to report to everyone that there are still many "Black Mermaids" in the world. Although they are black and not beautiful, they do not attract the attention of various people, so I have never seen any nautical tourists mention them, but when it comes to their art, it is also the art of swimming, which can not only be as beautiful as "mermaids," able to compare with fish, and can be called "mermaids," but also in some points, the art of "Black Mermaids" may even be higher than "mermaids." These "Black Mermaids" live in the seawater of the wharves of major commercial ports along the tropical line. Although not all of them are black people, they are generally black and shiny because they bathe in sunlight and seawater all year round. It can really be collectively referred to as "Black Mermaid." This kind of person already exists in Singapore, but the most outstanding ones are produced in "Qibu," a French colony on the east coast of Africa. They float naked in the sea and swim very fast and naturally. Their most special art is that they can sit steadily in the water without moving their hands and feet, sitting cross-legged as if sitting upright on land, but they can not sink. Ordinary swimmers have to rely on hand and foot movements to float, but they can sit and float in the water without making any gestures. "Qibu" is a port with huge winds and waves, but those "Black Mermaids" are not afraid of the winds and waves at all. When a big wave comes, they can rise and fall with the wave; even with the wave rolling, they can sit steadily on the peak of the wave. I am afraid that our "mermaid" cannot catch up with this kind of art. But all the "Black Mermaids" are not only not world-famous swimming stars, but are beggars who are played with. Whenever a ship arrives, they all gather around the ship to ask for money. Passengers on the ship throw silver coins into the water, and they can dive into the water and pick them up with their hands; some can even pick them up with their mouths. Sometimes they come on board and throw themselves into the water from a very high place to catch the silver coins thrown by the passengers. The passengers then use this to tease them and amuse themselves丨Swimming is originally an art, a sport, but now many people regard swimming as a profession. "Black Mermaids" are also good at this art, but this art has only become a means for them to beg for food in their hands. The same art also has distinctions of nobility and inferiority with the profession and identity!

Sculptor

— Feng Chi

There are many paths arranged for sculptors. In today's world where this kind of specialized talent does not seem to be too surplus, they should have relatively good prospects, right? A gilded sculptor can return to China and be a professor at a fine arts college. Taking three or four yuan an hour is not a rare thing; as for sculpting plaster statues or arranging showcases for people, it is even more inferior work. It would be a pleasing thing if they could associate with great people and celebrities and thus receive one or two copper statue business to do. The reward for a famous sculptor to cast a copper statue for someone will never be meager, with a minimum profit of five or six thousand yuan. Setting a price of around ten thousand or fifteen thousand yuan is not something unheard of. Naturally, a copper statue takes them more than half a year, but in general, their monthly income is still very considerable.

Regarding this kind of sculptor, I don't want to write too much about them. Below, I just want to briefly mention the lives of some students who come out of the sculpture department of fine arts colleges. These students do not have many good places to go. As a freelancer, they can naturally receive some sporadic small businesses to do. As for wanting to get a fixed position or seeking to obtain a big business, it is inevitable that it is a difficult-to-realize wish. Even if they really get something in this regard, the so-called position they get is nothing more than something to barely make a living. The so-called big business can be obtained by famous sculptors for ten thousand or eight thousand, but in their case, it is inevitable to be discounted again and again, reduced again and again, and ultimately they may not get half the amount of a famous sculptor. People even have to doubt whether his ability is enough, and even cancel the contract. It is worthy of people's sympathy that they suffer such discrimination with equal ability.

They can naturally also go to secondary schools to teach a few hours, and get a reward of five corners, eight corners, or one yuan per hour depending on the size of the school. They mostly understand a little painting, so in addition to teaching manual plaster practice, they can also teach painting. They can also arrange three-dimensional showcases in companies and shops, and get a fee of one or twenty yuan or two or thirty yuan per piece. They can also carve plaster statues for people, and the reward is difficult to determine, depending on the relationship between each other and the time required. There are also plaster statues of various styles carved for sale. To carve a plaster statue, you must first use a special kind of mud (said to be produced in Wuxi, and sold in stationery stores or craft shops near Shanghai Fine Arts School) to make a model, and a hollow mold is made from the model, from which many plaster statues can be cast. The procedure in between is naturally not very simple. Just in terms of utensils, there are many different sizes of bone, iron, and steel drills, chisels, knives, ...... and so on. The price of each plaster statue ranges from one or two yuan to two or twenty yuan.

Their better place to go is to go to a film company. They have many things to do in the film company, although the work may not all be in line with their profession. The most needed thing for film companies is to make "models." Sometimes these models are indispensable to film companies, but sometimes they are a way to cut corners. We know that the size of the image taken on the film is determined by the distance between the real object and the camera. If the camera is placed far away, large objects will become small on the film; if the camera is placed close, small objects will also appear large on the film. Based on this principle, film companies mostly do not completely build those sets that are difficult to build, have huge projects, and require a lot of expenses, but partially use some small models to replace them. These models, such as ships, trains, pagodas, palaces, city towers, fortresses, etc., are used in the same way as real ones because the proportions of the structure are uniform, and they can completely deceive the audience. If a ship catches fire or a giant building burns down, it is only necessary to burn some worthless model ships and model giant buildings. Isn't it more convenient and cost-effective?

There is also a kind of model, such as ancient heroes riding horses, which is sometimes needed, but if real people and horses in ancient costumes are actually dressed up and filmed, it is not only more costly and troublesome, but sometimes the result is not as pleasing as using models. However, doing this kind of thing in a film company is not necessarily a long-term nature. After a model is made, the company gets a reward of two or thirty yuan or three or forty yuan, and then they have to run for their future again.

However, in the film company, they can also do other things. For example, building three-dimensional sets or making subtitles is also often needed. Therefore, a sculptor who is not very successful but has some experience can always find some sporadic work in a film company. When the work of this company is completed, there is the work of that company waiting for him. With so many experiences, if there are excellent achievements, it is not entirely impossible to be given an actual position.

Art World

After Seeing the Hunan Fellow Villagers' Variety Show

— Zhou Min

丨A Grand Gathering of Hunan Film Stars and Singing and Dancing Stars丨

Almost everyone felt satisfied at the variety show held by the Hunan Fellow Villagers' Association to raise funds for primary schools in Shanghai. It not only brought together talent from Hunan's film and performing arts circles but also provided our drama with a new content and form of play adapting to this great gathering of talent: "Extra."

It's not easy to bring a sound film set to the stage, right? In the audience's ideals, they believe that the kingdom of art is full of freedom, happiness, and joy, but this here tells the audience a true scene. They—the extras—although they are indispensable figures in film work, they are always looked down upon and always forgotten by the audience. They exchange the lowest price for the longest working hours. They are veterans of playing the real life of society. In their chats, we can hear the truth of real life in modern society. In today's society, film has become industrialized, and they are the producers of this industrial production, but they live a miserable life of insufficient food and clothing.

The theme of this play is to express the real life of extras. The scene to be filmed on the set is a scene of the Volunteer Army fighting against the enemy and killing thieves. The Volunteer Army did not retreat due to the wounding of national heroes, and their efforts to kill the enemy were very realistic. However, this play ultimately transitions from the fake of filming to reality due to the limitations of form, then back to filming, and then back to reality, inevitably destroying the sense of reality of the drama. The components of the play within a play inevitably occupy a bit too much.

The playwright's technique is quite mature. He handles a scene of more than thirty people in such a way that everyone has a role. The protagonist of the play is Extra C, and the other characters also feel important. Extra C used to fight against the enemy in the Northeast and only became an extra because of the pressure of life, and the play being filmed is precisely about fighting against the enemy, so it often aroused his emotions. All of this is written very naturally. In the process of capturing two shots, the truthful content as described above is depicted, which cannot but be said to be a good harvest on today's desolate drama scene.

Thanks to the efforts of the director, Mr. Yun Wei, this complex scene has no confusion. Everyone's acting is very clear to the audience. The actors all worked hard and achieved considerable gains. Among them, Mr. Yuan Muzhi, the protagonist of "Peach and Plum Calamity" playing Extra C, was the most successful. Mr. Wan Laitian, who played the director, is originally a film director, and his performance is very suitable for the role. Mr. Xiao Ying, who played the manager, vividly portrays a typical representative of the boss. Ms. Hu Ping, who played the female star, also performed just right. Mr. Wei Heling, who played Extra A, although he has gained a lot, it is a pity that his rash actions weakened the climax. Other aspects, such as the grand and realistic scenery and the wonderful effects, also added a lot of color to the play.

In addition to the drama, there were also solo performances by Ms. Wang Renmei, Ms. Li Lili, Ms. Li Minghui, Ms. Hu Jia, Ms. Xu Lai, and song and dance programs by the Bright Moon Society, Plum Blossom Garden, and Xinhua Society. Unfortunately, I am too unprofessional when it comes to singing and dancing—naturally, I'm not that professional when it comes to drama either—so I can't say much. However, I always feel that the whole program is very clear, and the state of various goods being presented in a jumbled, redundant, and chaotic way is gone, which cannot but be regarded as progress in this variety show.

Amateur Entertainment

Mulian Play

— He

Mulian was a great disciple of the Buddha. He had great supernatural powers. Legend has it that he once went to hell to save his mother. The Ullambana Festival (held around the Ghost Festival in the seventh month of the lunar calendar), which is popular in various places today, originated from this story and has been evolved and spread. The "Mulian Saves His Mother" and "Grease Mountain" in old dramas also perform these well-known deeds. Mulian was a person who was extremely filial. In the past Chinese feudal society, he should have been regarded as a role model by those in power, and they would inevitably encourage the common people to emulate and admire him. The "Mulian Play" that I want to talk about here naturally also has the same unsound content: however, it is more detailed and stimulating in terms of script preparation and performance form.

Now I want to start with the story and structure of this play. Let's first examine the stories of the two plays "Mulian Saves His Mother" and "Grease Mountain" in Peking Opera, because they are related. Mulian's father, Fu the Wealthy, was a person who always did good deeds. One day, he saw a monk in front of his door eating a radish he had begged for. Before he finished eating, he fell to the ground and died. Fu the Wealthy took out money to buy a coffin for him. Later, Madam Liu dreamed of the monk again at night, and soon gave birth to a son, who was also named "Radish." Later, Fu the Wealthy passed away, and his son "Radish" became a monk. Madam Liu was grieved that the family of a virtuous person had been ruined, so she angrily broke all precepts, beat monks and scolded Taoists, drank alcohol and ate meat, offered meat oil to the Buddhist hall, demolished the Wanyuan Bridge, and did all kinds of things contrary to goodness. The King of the Underworld was furious when he learned of this and sent ghost messengers to take Madam Liu to the underworld, where she suffered all kinds of tortures such as the Mountain of Knives, the Tree of Swords, the Oil Pot, the Blood Pool, and the Grease Mountain. It is said that after Radish became a monk, he met the Buddha. The Buddha gave him the Dharma name Mulian, who had considerable Taoist practice; because he was very filial, he went to search for his mother, and later learned that his mother was suffering in hell after death, so he went to the underworld to save his mother, and traveled all over the ten halls and passed through the eighteen hells, and finally arrived at Fengdu City, where mother and son finally reunited. The play "Mulian Saves His Mother" usually only performs the part where mother and son meet in Fengdu, and "Grease Mountain" only performs the part where Madam Liu is about to suffer on Grease Mountain; while "Mulian Play" is performed in its entirety, and the plot is more complex than the above. "Mulian Play" starts with Fu the Wealthy's poor times, and then shows his development and promotion to prime minister, and his various good deeds, and his ascension to heaven after death, etc. The description of Madam Liu's all kinds of evil deeds is even more stimulating. Her abuse of monks and Taoists, the killing of animals, and her fierce and shrewish behavior are performed very vividly and lifelike. All kinds of pains in hell, such as frying in oil, casting lids, crossing the Bridge of Helplessness, and the Mountain of Knives and the Tree of Swords, are realistically set up on the stage, which is shocking to the audience. It can be seen that the story and structure of "Mulian Play" are more detailed and tighter than those of "Mulian Saves His Mother" in Peking Opera.

The performance scale of "Mulian Play" is also very large. "Mulian Play" has a total of seven major books and more than thirty scenes, which takes seven days and seven nights to complete. One book is played every day and night, and the performers should be given about 100 yuan of silver for the play, and food must also be provided. It is very common to spend nearly 1,000 yuan on a complete "Mulian Play" that takes seven days and seven nights, plus other expenses.

We can see from the number of actors required and the acting skills that the performance scale of "Mulian Play" cannot be compared with "Mulian Saves His Mother" in Peking Opera. "Mulian Play" requires a minimum of two people per scene, and large scenes require dozens to more than a hundred people. The number of actors can be increased to more than two hundred in the final reunion scene. Perhaps it is rare to see such a huge scene in Chinese folk drama performances? In terms of acting skills, the special abilities of the actors are also amazing. The performance emphasizes expressions, joy, anger, sorrow, danger, and tension, all of which are portrayed in detail. They have to shed real tears when they are sad, and they have to act as if they are in the situation when they are suffering. These are all very common. In addition, some people have to practice (or say they are divinely assisted) a kind of martial arts, like street performers, who can fly knives at a certain distance to the surroundings of another actor's head without harming him. The old master who teaches acting also has a set of skills, that is, before the main play begins, he has to chant spells to perform a set of magic, making a bamboo pole lying on the ground stand up by itself. This phenomenon is close to magic and superstition, but we still cannot fully explain this phenomenon. There are many such miraculous things in the performance process of "Mulian Play". Now I may as well give two more examples:

(1) "Searching for the House"丨The purpose of performing "Mulian Play" is to thank the gods, and entertainment is just a side effect. Anyone who is sick can make a wish to sing "Mulian Play", and even if the patient dies, they still have to sing it. "Searching for the House" means that one of the actors who plays the Wen Taishi goes to the altar of the people who are thanking the gods to chant spells and drive ghosts out of the "house." On this day, the people who are thanking the gods must eat vegetarian food and must not gamble, have sex, or do anything improper, otherwise disaster will come. When the Wen Taishi performs the magic, if he cannot speak fluently, then a misfortune will surely happen to this family this year. At this time, the whole family must kneel around him to reduce the harm. The gold powder on the face of the Wen Taishi can be sold for three or four yuan after removing the makeup.

(2) "Paralyzed Five Changs"丨When singing "Mulian Play", there are shrines for the five Chang gods in five places under the stage. During the performance, if one of them falls down, someone will definitely become unconscious and paralyzed and unable to speak. At this time, the old master must be invited to perform magic to heal them. After the healing, a reward of ten to twenty yuan must be given to the old master as a thank-you gift.

Naturally, these are all ridiculous tricks that are close to mythology. I personally do not believe that such strange things really happen, but because the people are ignorant and because this kind of play is deeply rooted in the hearts of the people, the people who are thanking the gods are always respectful and careful in carrying out their superstitious work.

Because the singing of Mulian Play costs a lot, the poor people certainly cannot afford to sing it, but the poor people are more likely to get sick, and they also have to "make a wish" to sing the play, so a kind of "small play" has emerged. This is similar to a kind of puppet show, but here the puppets used are idols of the Bodhisattva instead of puppets. The performance method is that the performers of "Mulian Play" hold the Bodhisattva idols in their hands and perform, singing and acting by themselves. This method costs less, and only about 20 yuan is needed each time. This kind of "small play" can also "search for the house" and drive away ghosts.

Legend has it that this kind of "Mulian Play" was compiled by Liu Ji (i.e. Liu Bowen) of the Ming Dynasty, and is now popular in Xuan City, Nanling, Jing County, Taiping and other counties in Anhui. The countryside of Wuhu and various counties in Huizhou also have performances of "Mulian Play". It is said that there is also a kind of "Mulian Play" in other provinces, such as Yixing in Jiangsu and Shaoxing in Zhejiang, but I don't know if its performance style is the same as what I said above. Liu Ji was originally from Qingtian County, Zhejiang. He was hired by Emperor Taizu of the Ming Dynasty to Jinling, and he made great contributions to assisting Emperor Taizu in achieving his imperial career. His works could have been spread to southern Anhui, southern Jiangsu, and eastern Zhejiang, but now there are too many myths about Liu Bowen among the people. Whether the author of this "Mulian Play" and the statement about its origin are based on conjecture is something we should suspect and deserves further investigation.

A Week's Travel Back to Hometown (4)

— Su Gang

As he spoke, he frowned for a while, then stretched his neck and busied himself back and forth on the bamboo mat on the boat for a while.

After the exhaustion of more than thirty people, this huge monster finally left Nanchang; at this time, layers of clouds had surged in the sky, wrapping the setting sun like rotten cotton, and the water surface reflected a strip of crimson brilliance. Seeing the current river scene, I couldn't help but think of Wang Bo's wonderful line "Autumn waters share one color with the long sky."

A few days of travel fatigue were exchanged for a wonderful dream scene; when I woke up the next day at one o'clock, half of the fatigue on my body seemed to have run away.

When the boatman saw me get up, he busied himself scooping a basin of washing water and said, "Old man! We don't have hot water here, so please make do with it!"

I looked into the wooden basin and couldn't help but shake my head, forcing myself to wash my face haphazardly.

The boatman took the washing water away and poured it out, then brought in the food; a bowl filled with dried-up peppers, and a bowl filled with coarse rice with grains, he set them out for me one by one, then said to me with a smile, "Old man, you have your own dishes, right! We only have these dishes here, and we won't change them until we get to Shangrao!"

"Do you eat this every day? Can you eat it?"

"If we don't eat this dish, there's no other dish to eat! Old man, please eat quickly, we're going to go into the water in front." He said, grinning again.

"Go into the water?" I asked in surprise.

"Yes! Old man, haven't you ever been on this kind of boat before? No wonder, you always have to go into the water when you're on this kind of boat." He said nonchalantly as usual.

Before I had finished my meal, I heard the boat owner shouting to the crew on the springboard, "Eat quickly! We've reached the shoal in front; hurry up and ask the guests to get off the boat!"

Many boatmen shouted in unison, and suddenly became busy again; the boatman who was delivering the food came in again to urge me, "Have you finished eating, old man? We've reached the shoal in front!"

"What should I do? It's going to be life-threatening to go into the water in this cold weather?" I said hesitantly, with a reluctant look on my face.

"Old man, there's no way around it, the boat is too heavy! Look! Aren't those guests in front all going down?" He had a bitter smile on his face, but his body was also shaking like a piano.

Looking at his shabby expression, and looking at the several guests who were already standing in the water, my heart couldn't help but soften; I encouraged myself and took off all the clothes from my lower body, followed the boatman to the bow of the boat, and slowly slipped into the water.

This huge monster seemed to be tired of walking and stopped there panting. The water was so clear that even a needle could be found. The stones the size of goose eggs at the bottom of the river were printed on the surface of the water, like a crystal glass pattern.

Opening Piece "Hearing the Bells"

Few people pass beneath Mount Emei. Bitter rain and cold winds beat against the face. The romantic emperor's feelings are endless. Imperial tears fall like rain for the jade beauty. Now, recalling the Hall of Eternal Life. The shadows of people and fragrance of clothes, the oath of the seventh evening. Wishing to be born together in the same bed, to die together in the same tomb. But now, where has her fragrant soul and beautiful spirit gone? The emerald phoenix and blue orioles are separated in two places. Teaching her to sing a song in the Pear Garden. The Rainbow Skirt Dance has lost its connoisseur. In the Pavilion of Submerged Fragrance, who will play Clear Peace with me? Chen Yuanli. Ruthless and heartless. Publicly compliant but secretly disobedient to me. Leading to the An Lushan rebellion in Fanyang City. From now on, it will be difficult to meet again. To see the virtuous concubine, I can only see white silk. Summon the strong man, open the box and bring me white silk. Seeing the silk is like seeing the face of the virtuous concubine. My concubine. It's not that I value the kingdom more than beauty. Gao Lishi enlighten the Holy Emperor. Lady Yang is already dead, how can she live again? Please urge the horses to rush along the winding mountain road. Hearing the bells at Jiange, my soul is broken. The cuckoo sings in the wind and rain, at the third watch of the night.

Supplement to Shen Bao This City Film Special

The Process of Adapting the Classic Novel "Treasure Island" by the Great British Writer Stevenson to the Silver Screen

Amidst the cleanliness movement, Hollywood production companies, in order to prevent difficulties from the Film Censorship Board and religious groups, are taking the most clever approach by using historical events and literary works as subjects for films. Therefore, recently in Shanghai cinemas, we have seen several films adapted from literary works, such as "Camille," depicting the great poet Byron, "The Count of Monte Cristo" by Alexandre Dumas, and "The Storm" by Ostrovsky. Recently, Nanjing will also publicly screen Stevenson's "Treasure Island."

The content of "Treasure Island" is entirely centered around pirates. Initially, the story was told by the author to his two children, but after publication, it became a literary classic, still popular among readers of various countries. Now, Stevenson's "Treasure Island," depicting the lives of pirates, has been adopted by MGM as the subject matter for a screenplay and adapted into a sound film, starring Wallace Beery and Jackie Cooper. Stevenson's two children, one named Lloyd Osbourne, has now become a famous writer, and the other, Isobel Osbourne, is now the wife of playwright and screenwriter Salibury Field. "Treasure Island" may have been produced by them.

Stevenson was a sickly writer. When he went to France for rest, he had already become a writer. Coincidentally, in France, he met Mrs. Osbourne of California, and they later married. Stevenson soon went to California and once lived in Calistoga and Monterey. In Monterey, he wrote many works. When he was in California, he told the story of "Treasure Island" to the two children of Mrs. Osbourne's previous husband. This story was published in London in 1883 and immediately became a timeless masterpiece. Now, this timeless masterpiece has been adapted to the silver screen. For the readers of this story, there are at least hundreds of millions of people who have read it and have deep impressions. Therefore, the production aspect naturally requires careful consideration. Director Victor Fleming handled everything very cautiously beforehand.

Screenwriter John Lee Mahin adapted "Treasure Island" into a screenplay, faithfully ensuring that the screenplay did not deviate from the original meaning, especially in the description of dialogue and actions. In "Treasure Island," the director did not focus on making the film's mood entirely based on action, but instead strived to follow Stevenson's descriptions. When "Treasure Island" was being filmed, special attention was also paid to the set design because every viewer who has read the original "Treasure Island" has a deep impression left in their mind of Stevenson's description of the "interior of the apple barrel," "the fence of the stockade," "the discovery of treasure," and "the exploration of the Hispaniola ship." Therefore, the handling of the scene must be particularly careful!

In the film "Treasure Island," everything regarding the scenery of pirate life and all the props, such as firearms, daggers, cannons, and other utensils, were designed by Darrel Franklin, who has been employed by the New York Museum and is a famous contemporary American writer of pirate novels. Perhaps when "Treasure Island" is publicly screened, every reader's childhood fantasies about "Treasure Island" will all become reality. In the film, Wallace Beery plays the pirate, Jackie Cooper plays the young boy, Lionel Barrymore plays the old captain, and there are more than a hundred unimportant supporting roles.

Film Reviews

Review of "Re-marriage" 丨丨 Xinguang

— Ji Han

American movies have a truly significant influence in China, which is universally acknowledged. Although "Re-marriage" is not entirely derived from American movies, some parts are influenced by them. We have seen "Idyll of the Fields" or other American movies that take materials from rural areas. The playwrights often contrast the simplicity of the countryside with the sins of the city, resulting in people clinging to the beautiful countryside and deeply hating the city, the source of evil. Naturally, this is not a correct concept, and in this regard, "Re-marriage" is no different from "Idyll of the Fields."

No, the main theme of "Re-marriage" is not in this area. What the playwright wants to show is the pitiful and ignorant old farmer, who has a son who does not learn well, resulting in a broken family and a miserable situation. However, on the other hand, we might as well reflect on it. If Gao Zhanfei, the character, did not study at a "wild chicken university" (naturally, the playwright deeply satirized the evils of education and the corruption of schools), he seemed to be able to study and become famous and become an official. In this way, he would not disappoint his old father, and his father would change from an old farmer to an old master. This point is probably an unforeseen side effect of the playwright.

In addition, we do not need to point out any greater significance in this film. What is pitiful is the old rich farmer, who wholeheartedly wants to rely on his son to make a name for himself, but has bad luck, and his son is useless. What can he do? As for spending four thousand yuan to become an official, the front door is sealed, but the back door can still be freely accessed, all of which are very realistic portrayals.

The director of "Re-marriage" has already shown some unique talent in "Wind" and is now demonstrating excellent skills here. He tells the story very clearly and concisely. He handles the atmosphere of the play very well, and the tone is also appropriate. Perhaps some say that there are some exaggerations, such as Xie Yunqing's encounter with all the prosperity and luxury when he arrives at his son's residence, which is a bit too contrived, and the description of Gao Qianping's temper is also a bit too exaggerated, making people feel like they are watching a play.

No problem, the director of this film is an excellent talent that our audience has high expectations for. However, excellent performance comes from the unity of content and form, and cannot exist solely on the technical aspect. That is to say, the director must decide his success on the entire work. Conversely, excellent technique does not express great and rich content, and its success is no more than that of a clever painter.

Finally, Yan Yuelan's performance as a social butterfly is more than competent. Gao Zhanfei and his wife were merely dutiful. The excellent cinematography added a lot to the beauty of the picture.

Review of "Success in Life"

— Wanshi (Stubborn Stone)

The Pursuit of Happiness

丨丨 Da Guangming

When feeling a lack of so-called subject matter, adopting readily available subject matter from novels or dramas has become the most convenient method for Hollywood. This "Success in Life" is another film adapted from a stage play.

Because it is derived from a stage play, it is always inevitably affected by the original work. For example, in the last scene, the appearance of a military officer allows several layers of difficulties and all the disputes to be eliminated. This kind of clever method is naturally not frequently found in modern dramas.

As a light comedy, it has had considerable success on the screen. Light, smooth, and bright, it makes people feel naturally happy. This is naturally very suitable for people who are tired and need to relax.

However, due to the decision of the story, other than achieving a sense of lightness and happiness, there are no other advantages. A comedy from the Washington era is truly too unfamiliar to us. Even if it accurately reflects the reality of that era, it does not give us a true and clear concept.

Audience Opinions

Talking about the Actors in "Plunder of Peach and Plum"

— Jing Yi

"Plunder of Peach and Plum" has already been publicly screened at Jincheng. The film journals in various newspapers have already published articles on its consciousness, skills, and structure for days. Whether it is successful or not, there will be fair criticism, so there is no need for me to say more. I will talk about several important actors who have transferred from the stage to the screen for the first time.

Chen Boer, who is praised as the "little angel," I still remember her playing the younger sister in "All Quiet on the Western Front." At that time, she gave me a very good impression. I believe she is a very promising person. Sure enough, in "Plunder of Peach and Plum," she proved that my words were not false. In this film, she plays the cousin Li Lilin, transitioning from a lively virgin to a woman's attitude. The shyness and innocence of a virgin, as well as the fatigue and exhaustion of a woman after giving birth, are quite successful, and the scene of falling from the stairs is especially realistic.

Yuan Meizhi is a member of the Xinyou Drama Society and the Drama Association. I saw him perform in "Roar, China!" During filming for "Plunder of Peach and Plum," he was very hardworking from beginning to end. From graduation to imprisonment, in the middle of the process, he increased the tragic elements in his voice, makeup, and performance, which helped to advance the entire play.

Tang Huaiqiu is a veteran of the spoken drama world. He has founded many drama societies and has also starred in famous plays such as "Suzhou Night Talk" and "The Landlady." In this film, he plays Principal Liu, with the demeanor of an old man, not inferior to the old painter in "Suzhou Night Talk." His facial expressions, his composure, his actions, and his voice all match the identity of the character in the play.

Zhou Boxun has always been known for playing wealthy businessmen or gentlemen and has previously starred in "L'Arlésienne." In "Plunder of Peach and Plum," he plays a lecherous manager, and the kind of disgusting and laughable expression, carrying satire in humor, is also very good.

About "Rebirth Flower"

— Huo (Fire)

"Rebirth Flower" is the sequel to "Sister Flowers" and is Zheng Zhengqiu's painstaking masterpiece of the year.

The plot of "Rebirth Flower" is more painful and moving than "Sister Flowers" and is more tortuous and graceful.

There is a scene in which Da Bao is rescued from prison by Er Bao and returns to her own home. She is changing the dressing for Tao Ge'er, who is wounded, when Xiao Zhang suddenly comes to inform her that the marshal has sent troops to arrest her. The poor family has to get up and flee in a panic. Zhao Dama does not want to burden Da Bao because she is old and sick and finds it extremely difficult to move, so she desperately asks Da Bao and Tao Ge'er to escape first, and she is willing to fall behind. However, how could Da Bao and Tao Ge'er agree? But Zhao Dama insisted that they leave first. As a result, everyone cried together and was arrested. When you see this scene, your heart cannot help but become anxious and sick, and you will have to shed tears silently. (But)

Film Novel

Golden Lotus Tribulation (Have a Heart) (5)

— Shumin

Early the next morning, Jimmy took Sally's dog to return it to her. Sally didn't expect him to come so early. When she saw Mei coming in, she hurriedly tried to hide her foot under her clothes, but it was already too late. She said with shame, "I really didn't expect you to come so early. I didn't want you to know." Jimmy smiled and comforted her, "Oh, oh, oh, oh. You not only look like an angel, but you also speak like an angel." He went over and hugged her. Sally became happy again. But her happiness was very short-lived. Suddenly, someone was knocking on the door outside. Sally went to open the door, and a man named Mike walked in. He was the one who lent the car to Jimmy yesterday. When Mike saw Jimmy, he told him that the company had been robbed last night and the police were now arresting him. When Jimmy heard his words, because he was originally honest and selfless, he refused to escape and waited quietly for the police to find him. After a while, sure enough, the company's manager, Xiao Boer, came with the police. Xiao Boer told Jimmy that if he paid back the money, he would not pursue the matter. Jimmy argued that he had not stolen the money from the company, but the police did not allow him to explain and took Jimmy away, locking him up. Sally felt heartbroken when she saw Jimmy being taken away by the police. She had to find a way to save him. She had to save him quickly, because if he was sentenced, he would have to serve two years in prison. She thought for a day and a night, and early the next morning, she ran to the manager Mr. Xiao Boer's place. When she saw the manager, besides the two of them, there was also the manager's secretary, Han Lun, organizing documents on the side. Sally pleaded in front of the manager, "What you said yesterday, if Jimmy returns the money quickly, you would be willing not to pursue the matter, right?" Xiao Boer nodded. Sally immediately opened her purse and put a large stack of banknotes on the table and said, "This is four hundred yuan... because I am afraid that he will be sentenced to imprisonment... please forgive him especially... please find a way to release him quickly... please..." Xiao Boer nodded. He said, "That's right. I'll call immediately." As he spoke, he grabbed the phone. Sally had a smile on her face as she left. She could no longer go to cut and treat her foot... she didn't know when she could cut and treat it, or if she would ever have the chance... but she saved Jimmy, this was something she secretly rejoiced in.

While Sally went to see the manager, Joan and Gates were visiting Jimmy in prison. When Jimmy saw them, he first anxiously asked about Sally, and then asked Gates, "Did you find that person?" Gates said, "I have already found the night watchman, but he doesn't have silver dollar tattoos on both arms." Jimmy felt very strange and said, "Really? Did you see clearly?" Gates said, "How could I not see clearly?" After a while, a police officer came in and told Jimmy that he could go out for a walk, he had been released. Jimmy was extremely happy to hear this. He immediately ran to the company, but as soon as he got to the company, he became angry because the manager told him that although he had been released, his crime had not been cleared. Jimmy then asked who had taken the money to bail him out, but the manager refused to tell him. Later, he got some news from Han Lun that it was Sally who had taken the money to bail him out. As a result, Han Lun deliberately added, "Isn't it strange? I never suspected that you would steal that money. But when Sally came to see Xiao Boer today, she seemed to know that you stole it." Jimmy jumped up, "You mean Sally knew I stole it?" Han Lun nodded, "Of course, I knew it from her tone." Jimmy heard this. He rushed to the door with anger and walked out. He went to question Sally. He ran to Sally's place and questioned her fiercely, asking if she had taken out the money to bail him out? Sally showed a very pitiful look and said, "The money was taken out by me, but I thought..." Jimmy shouted wildly, "You made everyone believe that I am a thief... everyone... you yourself believe it." Sally quickly argued with him, "No, no, no. That's not true." (To be continued)
